Talaq — Divorce
advanced
12 min
Establishing Lineage in a Conditional Divorce: Istihsan vs Qiyas
Intra-Hanafi dispute on lineage in conditional divorce

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on lineage in a conditional divorce scenario and explain why istihsan overrides qiyas.

Core Idea
Lineage is established by istihsan even when qiyas rejects it, because preserving lineage takes priority.

This passage addresses a rare but significant scenario: a man makes a conditional divorce before marriage, then marries and his wife gives birth exactly six months later. The Hanafi school, following Abu Hanifa, rules that the child's lineage is established and full mahr is due, based on istihsan (juristic preference) rather than strict qiyas. This lesson unpacks the reasoning, the intra-Hanafi disagreement, and the final relied-upon position.

Guided Path
1
Understand the hypothetical scenario
A man says 'If I marry so-and-so, she is divorced.' He marries her and she gives birth exactly six months after the marriage. Identify the key elements: the conditional divorce, the marriage, and the timing of birth.
2
Identify the Hanafi ruling and its basis
According to Abu Hanifa, the child's lineage is established and full mahr is owed. The basis is istihsan (juristic preference), which considers the rare possibility that intercourse coincided with the marriage contract.
The ruling is 'lazima nasabuhu wa mahruha' – his lineage and her mahr are established.
3
Analyze the qiyas objection
Zufar and Muhammad (in one opinion) argue by qiyas that since the divorce occurs immediately upon marriage, no valid intercourse could have taken place, so lineage should not be established.
This is the opposing qiyas argument: 'al-wat' fi hadha al-'aqd ghayr mumkin'.
4
Evaluate the istihsan response
The Hanafi response points out that the divorce is a consequence of the marriage and can be simultaneous with it. Conception can occur at the exact moment of marriage, before the divorce takes effect. Thus istihsan overrides qiyas because of the importance of lineage.
The passage even gives an extreme example: a man in the Maghrib marrying a woman in the East, and she gives birth at six months by a miracle – to show that pure intellectual possibility suffices.
5
Determine the mufta bihi and thamarah al-khilaf
The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is Abu Hanifa's: lineage established and full mahr wajib. The practical consequence (thamarah) is that the child is attributed to the father and the wife receives full mahr. The opposing view would deny lineage and reduce mahr.
The text also discusses a narration from Abu Yusuf suggesting one and a half mahr, but the preferred view is a single full mahr.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

(عيني، مستخلص، فتح) و مهرها [ أي لزم مهرها بتمامه. (ع)] لأنه لما ثبت النسب منه تحقق الوطء منه حكما وهو أقوى من الخلوة فتأكد به المهر، وفي القياس وهو رواية عن أبي يوسف يجب عليه مهر ونصف أما النصف فللطلاق قبل الدخول، وأما المهر كله فبالوطء حكماً أي لثبوت النسب والجواب: أنا إذا قدرنا أنه تزوجها حالة المواقعة لم تكن المواقعة بعد الطلاق فلا يلزمه إلا مهر واحد، وأيضاً الفعل واحد وقد اتصف بشبهة الحل فيجب مهر واحد، وفي "المنتقى": لا يكون به محصناً. Chapter on Establishing Lineage; i.e., explaining its rulings. Chapter on Establishing Lineage. ... And whoever says: 'If I marry her, she is divorced', then she gives birth after six months from when he married her, his lineage and her mahr are established. That is, if he says 'If I marry so-and-so, she is divorced' and then he marries her and she gives birth after six months from the marriage, the child is his son and he owes her mahr. As for the lineage, because she is his bed (firash); since she came with the child at six months from the time of marriage, she came with it at less than that from the time of divorce, so conception was before the divorce during the marriage. This can be conceived if he marries her while having intercourse, and the ejaculation coincides with the marriage contract, so conception occurs before the removal of the marriage bed (firash); because the divorce only occurs after the fulfillment of the condition, and the removal of the bed is the effect of the divorce, so it is simultaneous with it or after it. Although this scenario is rare, lineage is something that one goes to lengths to establish. Zufar said—and it was the first opinion of Muhammad—that his lineage is established, but this is qiyas; because intercourse in this contract is not possible due to the occurrence of the divorce before it without respite, so it must not be established. The basis of istihsan is what preceded: that it is possible that he marries her while he is intimately mixing, and the ejaculation coincides with the marriage, then the divorce occurs after that; because it is its consequence, and the consequence of a thing follows or accompanies it, so the conception is simultaneous with the removal of the bed. This is like the case of a man from the Maghrib who marries a woman from the East with a year's journey between them, and she gives birth at six months from the marriage because of intellectual possibility, that he could reach her by a miraculous step from Allah, or by having a flying mount. The birth was restricted to six months from the time of marriage because if she gives birth to it earlier, it indicates that conception preceded the marriage, so it is not established, and if she gives birth later, it indicates that she conceived after the divorce, so it is not established. (Ayni, Mukhtasar, Fath) And her mahr: i.e., her full mahr is owed. (Ayni) Because when the lineage from him is established, intercourse from him is proven legally, which is stronger than khalwa (seclusion), so the mahr is confirmed. In qiyas, and in a narration from Abu Yusuf, he owes one and a half mahr: the half for the divorce before consummation, and the full mahr for the legal intercourse (by establishing lineage). The answer: if we assume that he married her at the moment of intercourse, then the intercourse was not after the divorce, so only one mahr is owed. Also the act is a single act and it has acquired a semblance of halal, so one mahr is owed. In al-Muntaqa: it does not make him muhsin (one who has consummated a valid marriage). (Fath) The iddah of raj'i: i.e., the revocable divorce, and it includes the iddah by months or by periods, based on the presumption of menopause. And his saying: 'and if she gives birth after more than two years' is connected to what preceded, and it is established due to the possibility of conception during the iddah, due to the possibility that she has a long interval between periods. And there is no room to attribute it to zina or shubha (ambiguous intercourse) when pregnancy is possible. The implication of his statement is that if she gives birth to it earlier than that, his lineage is established even more so. -
Source pages p. 512

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute concerning the establishment of lineage when a man makes a conditional divorce statement before marriage. The scenario: a man says 'If I marry so-and-so, she is divorced', then he marries her and she gives birth exactly six months after the marriage. The ruling according to Abu Hanifa (istihsan) is that the child's lineage is established, and the full mahr is owed. The text explains the reasoning: although the divorce would occur upon fulfillment of the condition (marriage), it is possible that intercourse coincides with the marriage contract, so conception occurs before the divorce takes effect. Zufar and Muhammad (in one view) reject this, arguing by qiyas that since divorce is immediate upon marriage, no valid intercourse could have occurred; therefore lineage is not established. The Hanafi response relies on istihsan, allowing for the rare possibility of coinciding intercourse, similar to the analogy of a man marrying a woman at a great distance and she miraculously gives birth at six months. The passage then discusses the mahr: if lineage is established, he owes the full mahr. There is a narration from Abu Yusuf suggesting he owes one and a half (half for divorce before consummation plus full for legal intercourse), but the preferred view is a single full mahr because the act was simultaneously marriage and intercourse. Finally, the text addresses the iddah of a revocable divorce: if the woman gives birth after more than two years from the separation, lineage is still established due to the possibility of extended pregnancy, and this is even stronger if she gives birth earlier within two years.

Key Terms
علوق ('uluq): Conception; the moment the child is conceived.
فراش (firash): The marriage bed; legal presumption that a child born during marriage is attributed to the husband.
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference: a method of departing from qiyas for a stronger reason, such as necessity or custom.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the scenario where a man says 'If I marry so-and-so, she is divorced', then marries her and she gives birth exactly six months later, on what basis does Abu Hanifa establish the child's lineage?
A) Qiyas (analogy) because the marriage is valid and the divorce is separate.
B) Istihsan (juristic preference) because it is possible that intercourse coincided with the marriage contract.
C) Ijma (consensus) because all scholars agree on this point.
D) The literal text of the Quran that establishes lineage for any child born after marriage.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, lineage can be established by istihsan even when qiyas would reject it, prioritizing attachment of the child.

Talaq — Divorce

Conditional Divorce and Lineage at Six Months
Ruling with proof and intra-Hanafi dispute on conditional divorce lineage

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on establishing lineage when a conditional divorce coincides with marriage, and evaluate the qiyas vs. istihsan arguments.

Core Idea
Lineage is established via istihsan even if divorce occurs at marriage, as long as birth happens six months later.

This passage from the Hidayah addresses a rare but significant scenario: a man conditions divorce upon marriage, marries, and the wife gives birth exactly six months later. The Hanafi school, through Imam Abu Hanifa, upholds the child's lineage and full mahr based on istihsan, despite the apparent impossibility of intercourse. Here, we unpack the legal reasoning and the intra-Hanafi dispute.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and the ruling
The passage presents a man who says, 'If I marry you, you are divorced.' He marries her, and she gives birth exactly six months from the marriage date. The ruling: the child's lineage is established from him, and he owes full mahr.
Note the exact six-month condition; it is critical for the legal conclusion.
2
Understand the condition for lineage
Lineage is established only if the birth occurs exactly six months from marriage. If less, conception preceded marriage; if more, conception occurred after divorce. Both cases negate lineage.
The six-month period is the minimum gestation according to Hanafi fiqh.
3
Follow Abu Hanifa's istihsan argument
Abu Hanifa argues that conception could rationally coincide with the marriage contract if the man marries her while having intercourse, so ejaculation happens at the moment of marriage. The divorce only takes effect after the condition is fulfilled, thus after conception. This is a rare but intellectually possible scenario, so lineage is established via istihsan.
The analogy of a Westerner marrying an Easterner with a year's journey demonstrates that miraculous possibilities (e.g., jinn servant) can be considered.
4
Understand the opposing qiyas argument
Zufar and initially Imam Muhammad hold that lineage is not established. Their qiyas: intercourse at the moment of contract is impossible because the divorce occurs immediately upon marriage, eliminating the marital bed. Therefore, no conception can occur, so lineage fails.
This is a strict analogy to a normal divorce before consummation.
5
Apply the ruling to the mahr and note the special case
Once lineage is established, the wife receives full mahr because intercourse is legally confirmed (stronger than khalwa). A narration from Abu Yusuf suggests one and a half mahr (half for divorce before consummation plus full mahr for legal intercourse), but the accepted view is one mahr. Additionally, the husband is not considered a muhsin (one who has consummated) for purposes of hadd penalties.
The ruling on mahr shows the interplay between lineage and financial obligations.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن قال : إن نكحتها فهي طالق فولدت لستة أشهر مذ نكحها لزمَ نسبه ومهره أي إن نكحت فلانة أي فنكحها وولدت أي من حين لزم نسبه : أي نسب الولد منه عندنا استحساناً، ولو لأقل منها أو أكثر لم يثبت. أي من قال: إن تزوجت فلانة فهي طالق، فتزوجها فولدت ولداً لستة أشهر من يوم النكاح فالولد ابنه، وعليه مهرها، أما النسب؛ فلأنها فراشه؛ لأنها لما جاءت بالولد لستة أشهر عن وقت النكاح فقد جاءت به لأقل منها من وقت الطلاق فكان العلوق قبل الطلاق في حالة النكاح، ويتصور بأن تزوجها وهو يجامعها فوافق الإنزال النكاح، فيكون العلوق حاصلاً قبل زوال الفراش؛ لأن الطلاق لا تقع إلا بعد تمام الشرط، وزوال الفراش حكم الطلاق، فيكون مقارناً له أو بعده. وهذه الصورة وإن كانت نادرة إلا أن النسب مما يحتال لإثباته، وقال زفر وهو قول محمد أولاً: لا يثبت نسبه، وهو القياس؛ لأن الوطء في هذا العقد غير ممكن لوقوع الطلاق قبله من غير مهلة، فوجب أن لا يثبت نسبه، وجه الاستحسان ما سبق أنه يمكن ذلك بأنه تزوجها وهو مخالط لها فوافق الإنزال النكاح، ثم وجد الطلاق بعد ذلك؛ لأنه حكمه، وحكم الشيء يعقبه أو يقارنه، فيكون العلوق مقارناً لزوال الفراش، فصار كتزوج المغربي بالمشرقية، وبينهما مسيرة سنة فجاءت بولد لستة أشهر من يوم تزوجها للإمكان العقلي، وهو أن يصل إليها بخطوة كرامة من الله تعالى، أو أن يكون له استخدام وإنما قيد الولادة لستة أشهر من وقت التزوج؛ لأنها إذا جاءت به لأقل منه تبين أن العلوق كان سابقاً على النكاح، فلا يثبت، وإن جاءت به لأكثر منه تبين أنها علقت بعد الطلاق فلا يثبت أيضاً. ومهرها أي لزم مهرها بتمامه. لأنه لما ثبت النسب منه تحقق الوطء منه حكما وهو أقوى من الخلوة فتأكد به المهر، وفي القياس وهو رواية عن أبي يوسف يجب عليه مهر ونصف أما النصف فللطلاق قبل الدخول، وأما المهر كله فبالوطء حكماً أي لثبوت النسب والجواب: أنا إذا قدرنا أنه تزوجها حالة المواقعة لم تكن المواقعة بعد الطلاق فلا يلزمه إلا مهر واحد، وأيضاً الفعل واحد وقد اتصف بشبهة الحل فيجب مهر واحد، وفي "المنتقى": لا يكون به محصناً.
And whoever says: If I marry her then she is divorced, and she gives birth at six months from the time he married her, his lineage and her mahr are established. That is, if he says, 'If I marry so-and-so then she is divorced,' and he marries her and she gives birth to a child six months from the day of marriage, the child is his son, and he owes her mahr. As for lineage, because she is his bed; since she brought the child at six months from the time of marriage, she brought it at less than that from the time of divorce, so conception was before the divorce during marriage. It is conceivable that he marries her while having intercourse with her, and the ejaculation coincides with the marriage, so conception occurs before removal of the bed; because divorce only occurs after completion of the condition, and removal of the bed is the ruling of divorce, so it is simultaneous with it or after. This scenario is rare, but lineage is something one strives to establish. Zufar said - and it was Muhammad's first opinion: his lineage is not established, and this is qiyas; because intercourse in this contract is impossible due to the divorce occurring before it without delay, so it is necessary that his lineage not be established. The face of istihsan is what preceded: that it is possible that he married her while he was carousing with her, and ejaculation coincided with the marriage, then divorce occurred after that; because it is its ruling, and the ruling of a thing follows it or coincides with it, so conception coincides with removal of the bed. It becomes like a Westerner marrying an Easterner with a year's journey between them, and she gives birth at six months from the day of marriage, due to intellectual possibility - that he might reach her by a miraculous step from Allah, or he might have a jinn servant. The birth was restricted to six months from the time of marriage; because if she brings it at less than that, it becomes clear that conception preceded the marriage, so it is not established; and if she brings it at more than that, it becomes clear that she conceived after the divorce, so it is also not established. And her mahr: i.e., her full mahr is required. Because when his lineage is established, intercourse from him is legally confirmed, which is stronger than privacy (khalwa), so the mahr is confirmed. In qiyas, which is a narration from Abu Yusuf, he owes one and a half mahr: half for divorce before consummation, and all of the mahr for intercourse by legal implication (i.e., due to lineage establishment). The response: If we assume that he married her at the moment of intercourse, the intercourse was not after divorce, so he owes only one mahr. Also, the act is one and is characterized by a semblance of permissibility, so one mahr is owed. In al-Muntaqa: he is not considered a muhsin (one who has consummated) thereby.
Source pages p. 512

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling from the chapter on establishing lineage, specifically a case involving a conditional divorce. The ruling states that if a man says 'If I marry so-and-so, then she is divorced,' and he does marry her, and she gives birth exactly six months from the marriage date, then the child's lineage is established from him and the full mahr is due. The commentary explains the legal reasoning. The basis is that conception must have occurred before the divorce, since birth at six months from marriage means less than that from the divorce if the divorce occurred at marriage as per condition. The scenario is that the man marries her while already having intercourse, so the ejaculation coincides with the marriage contract, making conception occur while the marital bed is still intact; the divorce only takes effect after the condition is fulfilled, thus after conception. This is a rare but possible scenario. There is an intra-Hanafi dispute: Zufar and initially Imam Muhammad hold that lineage is not established (qiyas), because the intercourse at the time of contract is impossible given the divorce condition. Abu Hanifa uses istihsan, arguing that it is rationally possible (e.g., the miracle of a jinn servant). Therefore, lineage is established via istihsan. As for the mahr, normally divorce before consummation gives half mahr, but here since lineage is established, the full mahr is due. Abu Yusuf reportedly says one and a half mahr based on qiyas, but the accepted view is one mahr because the intercourse is legally confirmed. The passage also notes that in al-Muntaqa, such a man is not made a muhsin (i.e., does not have the status of one who has consummated) through this ruling.

Key Terms
نسب (nasab): Lineage; the legal attribution of a child to a father.
فراش (firāsh): The marital bed; the legal status of the wife being in a marriage that allows paternity.
علوق (ʿulūq): Conception; the moment the child is conceived.
استحسان (istiḥsān): Juristic preference; departing from qiyas for a stronger evidence or necessity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does Abu Hanifa establish lineage in the case of a conditional divorce where birth occurs six months after marriage?
A) Because the mother confirms the child is from the husband
B) Because it is rationally possible that conception coincided with the marriage contract before the divorce took effect
C) Because the husband admitted paternity
D) Because the child was born within the marriage period

Key Takeaway
Hanafi fiqh uses istihsan to establish lineage even in rare scenarios, prioritizing the preservation of nasab over strict qiyas.

Establishing Lineage from a Woman in 'Iddah: Raj'i vs Ba'in
Ruling on lineage establishment for child born in iddah of revocable and irrevocable divorce

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for establishing lineage for a child born to a woman in revocable and irrevocable iddah, and distinguish the rulings for each case.

Core Idea
Lineage is established for revocable iddah regardless of time; for irrevocable, only within two years.

The Hanafi school addresses lineage attribution for a child born to a woman in divorce iddah, with different rules depending on whether the divorce is revocable (raj'i) or irrevocable (ba'in). The key factor is the permissibility of intercourse during iddah and the maximum pregnancy period. This lesson explores the conditions and exceptions detailed in the classical texts.

Guided Path
1
Identify divorce type and its definition
Recognize whether the woman is in revocable (raj'i) or irrevocable (ba'in) iddah. This determines the permissibility of intercourse and the rules for lineage.
Raj'i: husband can revoke without new marriage. Ba'in: marriage ended permanently.
2
For raj'i: state the lineage rule and conditions
Lineage is established even beyond two years provided she does not acknowledge the end of her iddah. Also, the birth or intercourse may constitute a revocation (raj'a) if it occurs at two years or more.
3
For ba'in: state the lineage rule and conditions
Lineage is established only if birth occurs within two years. If at two years or more, not established because intercourse is haram and pregnancy cannot exceed two years.
The exact two-year case is disputed; some say it should be established.
4
Note the exception for twins and the intra-Hanafi dispute
If she gives birth to twins, one within two years and one beyond, Sheikhayn say both are attributed; Muhammad says only the first. The mufta bihi is the Sheikhayn view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويثبت نسب ولد معتدة الرجعي وإن ولدت لأكثر من سنتين ما لم تقر بمضي العدة وكانت رجعة في أكثر منهما لا في أقل منهما والبت لأقل منهما وإلا لا. وقيد بقوله: ما لم تقر بمضي العدة؛ لأنها إذا أقرت بانقضاء العدة ثم جاءت بولد لأقل من ستة أشهر ثبت نسبه لظهور كذبها، وإن جاءت لستة أشهر فصاعداً لم يثبت نسبه. وكانت رجعة: ضمير الفعل الناقص إلى الولادة في شرحي "الطائي" و"المسكين"، وفي شرح العيني: الضمير إلى الوطء، وعبارته هكذا: "وكانت وطئه اللازم من ثبوت النسب الواقع في العدة"، وهذا يقتضي أن الولادة أو الوطء لا تكون رجعة في السنتين فقط، أو الحكم في السنتين مسكوت عنه في عبارة المصنف، فيطلب حكمه من غير كتابه، فحيث وجد مصرح به يرجع إليه، ففي "الاختيار": "وإن جاءت به لسنتين أو أكثر كان رجعة"؛ لأن العلوق بعد الطلاق، والظاهر أنه منه، وأنه وطئها في العدة حملاً لحالها على الأحسن والأصلح، وهو نفي الزنا عنها، فيصير الزوج مراجعاً بالوطء في العدة من طلاق رجعي. لا في أقل منهما: أي لا يكون الميلاد أو الوطء رجعة إن جاءت به لأقل من سنتين؛ لأنه كما احتمل أن يكون العلوق بعد الطلاق احتمل أن يكون قبله فلا يكون مراجعاً بالشك؛ ولأنها بانت منه لانقضاء عدتها بوضع الحمل، وأورد أن للعلوق بعد الطلاق مرجحاً هو أن الظاهر أن الحوادث تضاف إلى أقرب أوقاتها، وأجيب بأن محله ما لم يعارضه ظاهر آخر وهو الوطء في العصمة لا في العدة، وفيه أيضاً مخالفة السنة في الرجعة بالوطء والعادة وهي الرجعة باللفظ فكان ما قضت به العادة والسنة أرجح. والبت بالجر عطف على قوله: معتدة الرجعي أي ويثبت نسب ولد معتدة الطلاق البت إذا ولدت منهما أي من السنتين؛ لأنه كان موجوداً عند الطلاق أو يحتمله فيحمل عليه. وإلا لا : أي وإن لم تأت بالولد لأقل من السنتين بل جاءت بسنتين أو أكثر لا يثبت نسبه؛ لأن وطئها بالعدة حرام، والحمل لا يبقى أكثر من سنتين فلا وجه لإلحاق النسب به كذا قيل وفيه أن هذا التعليل إنما يظهر إذا جاءت به لأكثر من سنتين؛ إذ الحمل حادث بعد الطلاق فلا يكون منه، وأما إذا جاءت به التمام سنتين فعدم ثبوته مخالف لما سيأتي من أن أكثر مدة الحمل سنتان؛ لأنه إذا جاءت به إلى السنتين لزم أن يكون العلوق سابقاً على الطلاق لعدم حل الوطء، وبه يلزم أن يكون الولد في بطن أمه أكثر من السنتين بخلاف غير المبتوتة لحل الوطء بعد الطلاق، قال في النهر ولزوم كون الولد في البطن أكثر ممنوع بأن يحمل على جعل العلوق في حال الطلاق؛ لأنه حينئذ قبل زوال الفراش. والمسألة مقيدة بما إذا لم تلد توأمين أحدهما لأقل من سنتين والآخر لأكثر منهما، فإن ولدتهما ثبت نسبهما منه عند الشيخين خلافاً لمحمد، ومقيدة أيضاً بأن لا تقر بانقضاء العدة، ثم هذا الحكم مخصوص بالمبتوتة المدخول بها،
And the lineage of the child of a woman in revocable iddah is established even if she gives birth after more than two years, as long as she does not acknowledge the passing of the iddah. And it (the birth or intercourse) is a revocation (raj'a) in more than two years, not in less than two years. And for the irrevocable (bā'in) divorce, (lineage is established) for less than two years, otherwise no. He restricted with his statement: 'as long as she does not acknowledge the passing of the iddah'; because if she acknowledges the expiration of the iddah and then brings a child at less than six months, his lineage is established due to the apparent falsity of her claim; and if she brings it at six months or more, his lineage is not established. 'And it is a raj'a': the pronoun of the defective verb (kānat) refers to the birth in the commentaries of al-Ṭā'ī and al-Miskīn; in Sharh al-'Aynī, the pronoun refers to intercourse, and his expression is: 'and it is his intercourse necessitated by the establishment of lineage occurring in the iddah.' This implies that the birth or intercourse is not a raj'a only in two years, or the ruling for two years is unmentioned in the author's expression, so its ruling is sought from other books. Where it is found explicitly, it is referred to. In al-Ikhtiyār: 'If she brings it at two years or more, it is a raj'a'; because conception after divorce, and the apparent is that it is from him, and that he had intercourse with her in the iddah, taking her situation as good and proper, which is negating adultery from her, so the husband becomes a revoker by intercourse in the iddah from a revocable divorce. 'Not in less than two years': i.e., the birth or intercourse is not a raj'a if she brings it at less than two years; because just as it is possible that conception was after divorce, it is possible that it was before, so he does not become a revoker due to doubt; and because she becomes separated from him by the end of her iddah upon delivery. It was argued that conception after divorce has a preponderance: the apparent is that events are attributed to their nearest times. The answer: that is where there is no other apparent contradiction, which is intercourse within the bond (not in iddah). Also, it violates the sunna of revocation by intercourse and the custom which is revocation by verbal statement, so what custom and sunna dictated is more preponderant. 'And al-batt' (irrevocable) is genitive, conjoined to 'revocable iddah': i.e., the lineage of the child of a woman in irrevocable divorce iddah is established if she gives birth (within) from the two years, i.e., less than two years; because (the child) was present at the time of divorce or possibly so, so it is attributed to him. 'Otherwise no': i.e., if she does not bring the child at less than two years, but brings it at two years or more, his lineage is not established; because intercourse with her in iddah is haram, and pregnancy does not remain more than two years, so there is no basis for attaching lineage to him, as is said. But there is in this that this reasoning only appears if she brings it at more than two years; because the pregnancy occurred after divorce so it is not from him. But if she brings it exactly at two years, then its non-establishment contradicts what will come that the maximum period of pregnancy is two years; because if she brings it at two years, it would necessitate that conception preceded divorce due to the impermissibility of intercourse, and that would make the child in her womb more than two years, unlike the non-bā'in (i.e., raj'i) woman due to permissible intercourse after divorce. An-Nahr says: The necessity of the child being in the womb for more than two years is prevented by interpreting that conception occurred at the moment of divorce; because then it was before the removal of the bed. And the issue is restricted to when she does not give birth to twins, one less than two years and the other more than two years; if she gives birth to both, their lineage is established from him according to the two shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf), contrary to Muhammad. And it is also restricted to her not acknowledging the expiration of the iddah. Then this ruling is specific to the bā'in woman who was consummated upon.
Source pages p. 512

Commentary
This passage handles lineage for a child born to a woman undergoing 'iddah. There are two categories: revocable (raj'i) divorce and irrevocable (ba'in) divorce. For the revocable divorce, lineage is established even if the child is born more than two years after the divorce, as long as the woman does not affirm that her 'iddah has ended. The reason is that intercourse during 'iddah is permissible for the husband (since he can revoke), so the child can be attributed to him. If she acknowledges the end of 'iddah and then gives birth at less than six months from that acknowledgment, lineage is established because her claim is false. If she gives birth at six months or more, it is not established. The passage also discusses whether the birth or intercourse itself constitutes a revocation (raj'a). If the birth occurs at two years or more, it is considered a revocation according to al-Ikhtiyar, because the apparent is that intercourse happened during 'iddah, so the husband's action is a revocation. If less than two years, it is not a revocation due to possibility of conception before divorce and because she is separated upon delivery. For the ba'in (irrevocable) divorce, lineage is established only if the child is born less than two years from the divorce. This is because after ba'in divorce, intercourse is haram, so if the child is born at two years or more, it cannot be attributed to the husband since pregnancy cannot exceed two years (allegedly). There is a dispute about the two-year exact mark: some say it should be attributed. The passage restricts the ruling to cases where the woman does not give birth to twins with different timings, and where she does not acknowledge the end of 'iddah. Also, the ruling applies only to a woman in ba'in divorce who was consummated upon.

Key Terms
عدة (ʿiddah): The waiting period a woman must observe after divorce or death of husband before remarrying.
رجعي (rajʿī): Revocable divorce; the husband can take back his wife during the iddah without a new contract.
بت (batt): Irrevocable divorce; the marriage ends permanently, and the husband cannot revoke.
رجعة (rajʿah): Revocation; the act of taking back one's wife during iddah of a revocable divorce.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In a ba'in (irrevocable) divorce, why is lineage not established if the woman gives birth at exactly two years?
A) Because the marriage contract has ended and intercourse is permissible only during iddah
B) Because the maximum pregnancy period is two years and if birth occurs at two years, conception must have been before divorce, but since intercourse is haram after ba'in, it cannot be from the husband
C) Because the woman must acknowledge the end of iddah
D) Because the child is illegitimate by default

Key Takeaway
For revocable divorce, lineage is established regardless of time unless she acknowledges end of iddah; for irrevocable divorce, only if birth occurs within two years.

Lineage after Revocable Divorce: Conditions for Raj'ah and Birth Timing
Establishes rules for lineage based on birth timing and confession.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which a birth after revocable divorce establishes lineage and identify when it constitutes a revocable return (raj'ah).

Core Idea
Birth within two years after revocable divorce establishes lineage and counts as raj'ah, unless the woman confesses iddah expiry.

The previous lesson introduced the general rules of iddah. Now we examine a specific scenario: when a divorced woman gives birth after the divorce. The Hanafi school has detailed rules determining whether the child's lineage is established and whether the husband's action (intercourse or birth itself) constitutes a revocable return to the marriage. Understanding these rules requires careful attention to timing and the wife's statements.

Guided Path
1
Identify the divorce type
First, determine whether the divorce is revocable (raj'i) or irrevocable (ba'in). The rules differ. The text begins with the revocable case.
The passage uses 'العدة، وكانت رجعة' to refer to the revocable scenario.
2
Check birth timing
For revocable divorce, the ruling depends on whether the birth occurs within two years of the divorce, exactly at two years, or beyond. If within two years (but not at the exact two-year mark), the birth constitutes a revocable return by intercourse, and lineage is established.
The phrase 'في أكثر منهما' means more than two years; the author clarifies that less than two years is not a return.
3
Consider the wife's confession
If the wife confesses that her 'iddah has expired before the birth, the ruling changes. If she gives birth less than six months after that confession, lineage is established due to her lie. If six months or more, lineage is not established.
The text says: 'ما لم تقر بمضي العدة' – this condition overrides the general two-year rule.
4
Identify the ruling for exactly two years
The author notes that the ruling for birth exactly at two years is not in the base text but is found in other works like al-Ikhtiyar. There, it is considered a revocable return and lineage is established.
This shows the need to consult multiple sources within the Hanafi school.
5
Apply the rule for lineage establishment
After applying the above conditions, conclude whether the child's lineage is attributed to the husband. The act of birth (or intercourse) that constitutes raj'ah is considered a revocable return.
The lineage is established (nasab thabit) unless a condition fails.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب ثبوت النسب

أي الولادة عليها إذا كان الميلاد السنتين
أي من السنتين
- وقيد بقوله: "ما لم تقر بمضي العدة؛ لأنها إذا أقرت بانقضاء العدة ثم جاءت بولد لأقل من ستة أشهر ثبت نسبه لظهور كذبها، وإن جاءت لستة أشهر فصاعداً لم يثبت نسبه. (فتح) بمضي العدة: فلو أقرت بانقضائها ثم جاءت به لستة أشهر فصاعداً لم يثبت. (ع) وكانت رجعة: ضمير الفعل الناقص إلى الولادة في شرحي "الطائي" و"المسكين"، وفي شرح العيني: الضمير إلى الوطء، وعبارته هكذا: "وكانت وطئه اللازم من ثبوت النسب الواقع في العدة"، وهذا يقتضي أن الولادة أو الوطء لا تكون رجعة في السنتين فقط، أو الحكم في السنتين مسكوت عنه في عبارة المصنف، فيطلب حكمه من غير كتابه، فحيث وجد مصرحاً به يرجع إليه، ففي "الاختيار": "وإن جاءت به لسنتين أو أكثر كان رجعة"؛ لأن العلوق بعد الطلاق، والظاهر أنه منه، وأنه وطئها في العدة حملاً لحالها على الأحسن ،والأصلح، وهو نفي الزنا عنها، فيصير الزوج مراجعاً بالوطء في العدة من طلاق رجعي. (مستخلص، فتح)
لا في أقل منهما : أي لا يكون الميلاد أو الوطء رجعة إن جاءت به لأقل من سنتين؛ لأنه كما احتمل أن يكون العلوق بعد الطلاق احتمل أن يكون قبله فلا يكون مراجعاً بالشك؛ ولأنها بانت منه لانقضاء عدتها بوضع الحمل، وأورد أن للعلوق بعد الطلاق مرجحاً هو أن الظاهر أن الحوادث تضاف إلى أقرب أوقاتها، وأجيب بأن محله ما لم يعارضه ظاهر آخر وهو الوطء في العصمة لا في العدة، وفيه أيضاً مخالفة السنة في الرجعة بالوطء والعادة وهي الرجعة باللفظ فكان ما قضت به العادة والسنة أرجح. (مستخلص، فتح)
والبت بالجر عطف على قوله: معتدة الرجعي أي ويثبت نسب ولد معتدة الطلاق البت إذا ولدت. (ع) منهما : أي من السنتين؛ لأنه كان موجوداً عند الطلاق أو يحتمله فيحمل عليه. (ع) وإلا لا : أي وإن لم تأت بالولد لأقل من السنتين بل جاءت بسنتين أو أكثر لا يثبت نسبه؛ لأن وطئها بالعدة حرام، والحمل لا يبقى أكثر من سنتين فلا وجه لإلحاق النسب به كذا قيل وفيه أن هذا التعليل إنما يظهر إذا جاءت به لأكثر من سنتين؛ إذ الحمل حادث بعد الطلاق فلا يكون منه، وأما إذا جاءت به التمام سنتين فعدم ثبوته مخالف لما سيأتي من أن أكثر مدة الحمل سنتان؛ لأنه إذا جاءت به إلى السنتين لزم أن يكون العلوق سابقاً على الطلاق لعدم حل الوطء، وبه يلزم أن يكون الولد في بطن أمه أكثر من السنتين بخلاف غير المبتوتة لحل الوطء بعد الطلاق، قال في النهر ولزوم كون الولد في البطن أكثر ممنوع بأن يحمل على جعل العلوق في حال الطلاق؛ لأنه حينئذ قبل زوال الفراش. والمسألة مقيدة بما إذا لم تلد توأمين أحدهما لأقل من سنتين والآخر لأكثر منهما، فإن ولدتهما ثبت نسبهما منه عند الشيخين خلافاً لمحمد، ومقيدة أيضاً بأن لا تقر بانقضاء العدة، ثم هذا الحكم مخصوص بالمبتوتة المدخول بها.
Chapter of Establishing Lineage. The waiting period, and it is a revocable return in more than both, not in less than both, and the irrevocable divorce is for less than both. Meaning: the birth upon her if the birth is within two years. Meaning: from the two years. And he restricted by his saying: 'As long as she does not confess the passing of the waiting period; because if she confesses the expiry of the waiting period then gives birth to a child in less than six months, his lineage is established due to the appearance of her lie, but if she gives birth in six months or more, his lineage is not established (Fath). By the passing of the waiting period: if she confesses its expiry then gives birth to it in six months or more, it is not established (Ayni). And 'it is a revocable return': the pronoun of the defective verb refers to childbirth in the commentaries of al-Ta'i and al-Miskin, and in Sharh al-Ayni: the pronoun refers to intercourse, and his expression is: 'And it is his intercourse necessitated by the establishment of lineage occurring in the waiting period.' This implies that childbirth or intercourse does not constitute a revocable return only in the two years, or the ruling regarding the two years is unmentioned in the author's expression, so its ruling is sought from other than his book; wherever it is found explicitly stated, one refers to it. Thus in al-Ikhtiyar: 'And if she brings it in two years or more, it is a revocable return'; because the conception after the divorce, and the apparent is that it is from him, and that he had intercourse with her in the waiting period, carrying her situation upon the best and most appropriate, which is negating adultery from her, so the husband becomes a revocable returner by intercourse in the waiting period from a revocable divorce (Mukhtalaf, Fath). 'Not in less than both': meaning: the birth or intercourse is not a revocable return if she brings it in less than two years; because just as it is possible that the conception was after the divorce, it is possible it was before, so he does not become a returner due to doubt; and because she becomes irrevocably separated from him by the expiry of her waiting period due to delivery. And it was objected that for conception after the divorce there is a preponderant factor: that the apparent is that events are attributed to their nearest times. And it was answered: its place is where another apparent does not contradict it, which is intercourse in the bond of marriage not in the waiting period. And it also contains violation of the sunnah regarding the revocable return by intercourse, and the custom is the revocable return by speech, so what custom and sunnah dictated is more preponderant (Mukhtalaf, Fath). 'And the irrevocable' in genitive is conjuncted to his saying: 'a revocable waiting-period woman', meaning: the lineage of the child of a woman in irrevocable divorce waiting period is established if she gives birth (Ayni). 'From them': meaning from the two years; because he was present at the time of divorce or it is possible, so it is attributed to him (Ayni). 'And if not, no': meaning: if she does not bring the child in less than two years, but brings it in two years or more, his lineage is not established; because intercourse with her during the waiting period is unlawful, and pregnancy does not last more than two years, so there is no basis for attributing lineage to him, as was said. But there is that this reasoning only appears if she brings it in more than two years; since the pregnancy occurs after the divorce, it cannot be from him. But if she brings it exactly at two years, its non-establishment contradicts what will come that the maximum duration of pregnancy is two years; because if she brings it at two years, it would necessitate that the conception preceded the divorce due to the unlawfulness of intercourse, and thus it would necessitate that the child was in the mother's womb for more than two years, unlike the non-irrevocably divorced woman due to the lawfulness of intercourse after divorce. He said in al-Nahr: The necessity of the child being in the womb longer is denied by assuming the conception at the time of divorce; because then it is before the removal of the marriage bed. And the issue is restricted to if she did not give birth to twins, one in less than two years and the other in more than two years; if she gives birth to them, their lineage is established from him according to the two shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf), contrary to Muhammad. And it is also restricted to her not confessing the expiry of the waiting period. Then this ruling is specific to the irrevocably divorced woman who has been consummated with.
Source pages p. 513

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the rules of establishing lineage (nasab) for a child born after a divorce. The author first discusses the revocable (raj'i) divorce: if the wife gives birth within two years from the divorce, the birth is considered a revocable return (رجعة) by intercourse, and the child's lineage is established. If more than two years, it is not a return and lineage is not established. If less than two years but she confesses that her 'iddah has expired, then if she gives birth in less than six months from that confession, lineage is established because her lie is evident; if six months or more, it is not. The commentary explains grammatical points about the pronoun reference and notes that the ruling for exactly two years is taken from other works like al-Ikhtiyar, where it is considered a return. For an irrevocable (ba'in) divorce, specifically the consummated woman, lineage is established if birth occurs within two years from divorce, because the child could have been conceived before the divorce. If more than two years, lineage is not established, with detailed discussion about the maximum pregnancy duration being two years. There is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding twins: if one twin is born within two years and the other after, both are attributed to the husband according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf (the Sheikhayn), contrary to Muhammad al-Shaybani. The whole ruling is conditioned on the woman not confessing that her 'iddah has expired.

Key Terms
الرجعة (al-raj'ah): In this context, the revocable return of the husband to his wife during the 'iddah period, either by word or by intercourse, reinstating the marriage without a new contract.
البت (al-bat): Irrevocable divorce (ba'in), especially with three pronouncements, after which the husband cannot take back the wife without a new marriage and consummation with another man.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
For a revocable divorce, what is the maximum time after divorce for a birth to be considered a revocable return (raj'ah) and establish lineage, if the woman never confesses iddah expiry?
A) Six months.
B) One year.
C) Two years (including exactly two years per al-Ikhtiyar).
D) Unlimited time.

Key Takeaway
For revocable divorce, the child's lineage is established if born within two years (or exactly two years per al-Ikhtiyar), and the birth itself becomes a revocable return (raj'ah), provided the wife does not confess iddah expiry.

Lineage after Irrevocable Divorce: Two-Year Rule and Twin Dispute
Establishes rules for lineage based on birth timing and confession.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the two-year rule for lineage after irrevocable divorce and state the difference between the Sheikhayn and Imam Muhammad on the twin case.

Core Idea
Irrevocable divorce: lineage established only if birth within two years; twins born across the two-year mark are both attributed according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf.

The previous lesson dealt with revocable divorce. Now we turn to irrevocable (ba'in) divorce, which has a stricter rule: intercourse after divorce is unlawful, so lineage is only established if the child could have been conceived before the divorce. The maximum pregnancy period of two years is critical, and there is a famous intra-Hanafi dispute on twins. Understanding this ikhtilaf is essential for knowing the mufta bihi (operative position) in the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the divorce type as irrevocable
The text discusses 'المبتوتة' (the irrevocably divorced woman) after consummation. This is a key distinction from revocable divorce.
The phrase 'والبائنة' is connected to the earlier discussion.
2
Apply the two-year maximum pregnancy rule
For an irrevocably divorced woman, the child's lineage is established only if the birth occurs within two years of the divorce. This is because the maximum pregnancy is two years, and any child born after that could not have been conceived before the divorce.
The text says: 'وإلا لا' – if not within two years, lineage is not established.
3
Consider the exception for twins
The text specifically mentions an exception: if the woman gives birth to twins, one within two years and one after two years, the ruling depends on which Hanafi authority you follow.
'فإن ولدتهما ثبت نسبهما منه عند الشيخين خلافاً لمحمد'
4
Analyze the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
According to the Sheikhayn (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf), both twins are attributed to the husband. Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani disagrees and holds that only the twin born within two years is attributed.
This is an example of legitimate ikhtilaf within the Hanafi school.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The text implies that the view of the Sheikhayn is preferred (as they are the majority and the case is mentioned in their favor). The mufta bihi is the attribution of both twins.
Many later Hanafi works adopt the Sheikhayn's view.

(مستخلص، فتح)

Chapter of Establishing Lineage. The waiting period, and it is a revocable return in more than both, not in less than both, and the irrevocable divorce is for less than both. Meaning: the birth upon her if the birth is within two years. Meaning: from the two years. And he restricted by his saying: 'As long as she does not confess the passing of the waiting period; because if she confesses the expiry of the waiting period then gives birth to a child in less than six months, his lineage is established due to the appearance of her lie, but if she gives birth in six months or more, his lineage is not established (Fath). By the passing of the waiting period: if she confesses its expiry then gives birth to it in six months or more, it is not established (Ayni). And 'it is a revocable return': the pronoun of the defective verb refers to childbirth in the commentaries of al-Ta'i and al-Miskin, and in Sharh al-Ayni: the pronoun refers to intercourse, and his expression is: 'And it is his intercourse necessitated by the establishment of lineage occurring in the waiting period.' This implies that childbirth or intercourse does not constitute a revocable return only in the two years, or the ruling regarding the two years is unmentioned in the author's expression, so its ruling is sought from other than his book; wherever it is found explicitly stated, one refers to it. Thus in al-Ikhtiyar: 'And if she brings it in two years or more, it is a revocable return'; because the conception after the divorce, and the apparent is that it is from him, and that he had intercourse with her in the waiting period, carrying her situation upon the best and most appropriate, which is negating adultery from her, so the husband becomes a revocable returner by intercourse in the waiting period from a revocable divorce (Mukhtalaf, Fath). 'Not in less than both': meaning: the birth or intercourse is not a revocable return if she brings it in less than two years; because just as it is possible that the conception was after the divorce, it is possible it was before, so he does not become a returner due to doubt; and because she becomes irrevocably separated from him by the expiry of her waiting period due to delivery. And it was objected that for conception after the divorce there is a preponderant factor: that the apparent is that events are attributed to their nearest times. And it was answered: its place is where another apparent does not contradict it, which is intercourse in the bond of marriage not in the waiting period. And it also contains violation of the sunnah regarding the revocable return by intercourse, and the custom is the revocable return by speech, so what custom and sunnah dictated is more preponderant (Mukhtalaf, Fath). 'And the irrevocable' in genitive is conjuncted to his saying: 'a revocable waiting-period woman', meaning: the lineage of the child of a woman in irrevocable divorce waiting period is established if she gives birth (Ayni). 'From them': meaning from the two years; because he was present at the time of divorce or it is possible, so it is attributed to him (Ayni). 'And if not, no': meaning: if she does not bring the child in less than two years, but brings it in two years or more, his lineage is not established; because intercourse with her during the waiting period is unlawful, and pregnancy does not last more than two years, so there is no basis for attributing lineage to him, as was said. But there is that this reasoning only appears if she brings it in more than two years; since the pregnancy occurs after the divorce, it cannot be from him. But if she brings it exactly at two years, its non-establishment contradicts what will come that the maximum duration of pregnancy is two years; because if she brings it at two years, it would necessitate that the conception preceded the divorce due to the unlawfulness of intercourse, and thus it would necessitate that the child was in the mother's womb for more than two years, unlike the non-irrevocably divorced woman due to the lawfulness of intercourse after divorce. He said in al-Nahr: The necessity of the child being in the womb longer is denied by assuming the conception at the time of divorce; because then it is before the removal of the marriage bed. And the issue is restricted to if she did not give birth to twins, one in less than two years and the other in more than two years; if she gives birth to them, their lineage is established from him according to the two shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf), contrary to Muhammad. And it is also restricted to her not confessing the expiry of the waiting period. Then this ruling is specific to the irrevocably divorced woman who has been consummated with.
Source pages p. 513

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the rules of establishing lineage (nasab) for a child born after a divorce. The author first discusses the revocable (raj'i) divorce: if the wife gives birth within two years from the divorce, the birth is considered a revocable return (رجعة) by intercourse, and the child's lineage is established. If more than two years, it is not a return and lineage is not established. If less than two years but she confesses that her 'iddah has expired, then if she gives birth in less than six months from that confession, lineage is established because her lie is evident; if six months or more, it is not. The commentary explains grammatical points about the pronoun reference and notes that the ruling for exactly two years is taken from other works like al-Ikhtiyar, where it is considered a return. For an irrevocable (ba'in) divorce, specifically the consummated woman, lineage is established if birth occurs within two years from divorce, because the child could have been conceived before the divorce. If more than two years, lineage is not established, with detailed discussion about the maximum pregnancy duration being two years. There is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding twins: if one twin is born within two years and the other after, both are attributed to the husband according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf (the Sheikhayn), contrary to Muhammad al-Shaybani. The whole ruling is conditioned on the woman not confessing that her 'iddah has expired.

Key Terms
الرجعة (al-raj'ah): In this context, the revocable return of the husband to his wife during the 'iddah period, either by word or by intercourse, reinstating the marriage without a new contract.
البت (al-bat): Irrevocable divorce (ba'in), especially with three pronouncements, after which the husband cannot take back the wife without a new marriage and consummation with another man.
التوأم (al-taw'am): Twin; multiple children from a single pregnancy.
الشيخين (al-Shaykhayn): The two shaykhs: Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf. In Hanafi literature, this term usually refers to these two imams, as Muhammad al-Shaybani is often distinguished.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on the lineage of twins born to an irrevocably divorced woman, when one twin is born within two years and the other after two years?
A) Both twins are attributed to the husband according to all Hanafi imams.
B) Only the first twin is attributed, according to all Hanafi imams.
C) Both are attributed according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, but only the first according to Muhammad.
D) Neither twin is attributed because the second is born after two years.

Key Takeaway
In irrevocable divorce, birth within two years establishes lineage; for twins spanning the two-year mark, the mufta bihi (Sheikhayn's view) attributes both children to the husband.

Talaq — Divorce
intermediate
10 min
Husband's Claim and Minor Wife in Lineage Establishment
Ruling with two exceptions and intra-Hanafi dispute on timeframe

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which a husband's claim establishes lineage and calculate the timeframe for a divorced minor wife.

Core Idea
Lineage from a divorced minor wife is only established within nine months; the husband's claim requires a valid shubhah involving both act and contract.

This lesson continues the discussion on lineage (nasab) by examining two key exceptions: the husband's claim of paternity after divorce, and the special case of a divorced minor girl (murahaqah). The Hanafi school distinguishes between types of shubhah (mistaken belief) that can support such claims, and imposes strict time limits to ensure certainty. We will unpack the reasoning behind these rulings and the intra-Hanafi disagreement over the maximum period.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two exceptional cases
Recognize that the text provides an exception from the general rule that lineage is not established: (a) when the husband claims the child, and (b) the case of a divorced minor wife if born within a specific period.
2
Analyze the husband's claim and shubhah
Understand that the claim is valid only if based on a shubhah that is not purely act-based. A purely act-based shubhah (e.g., intercourse with a slave-girl) does not suffice; a shubhah with a contractual element (e.g., thinking the divorce was revocable) does. Also note whether the wife's confirmation is required—the preferred view is that it is not.
The text discusses this through an objection and answer.
3
Determine the timeframe for a divorced minor wife
For a consummated minor (murahaqah), the period is nine months from divorce: three months 'iddah plus six months minimum pregnancy. For an unconsummated minor, it is six months. This applies only if the wife has not confessed the expiry of her 'iddah.
If she confesses expiry, the calculation changes.
4
Evaluate the intra-Hanafi dispute
Compare the majority view (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad: nine months maximum) with Abu Yusuf's view (up to two years for irrevocable divorce, up to twenty-seven months for revocable). Identify the practical consequence: if a child is born between nine months and two years, lineage is established according to Abu Yusuf but not according to the majority.
The text sides with the majority: 'عند الطرفين'.

Except that he claims it, and the minor girl for less than nine months, and if not, no. Meaning: the husband because he accepted it. If she was not consummated with and she brings a child in six months or more from the time of separation, lineage is not established; if she brings it in less than six months from the time of separation, it is established (Mukhtalaf, Fath). 'Except that he claims it' is an absolute exception from his saying: 'and if not, no', meaning lineage is not established in any case except in the case of the husband's claim; because he accepted it, and for the establishment of lineage there is a basis that he had intercourse with her under mistaken belief (shubha) in the waiting period, such as thinking she was his other wife and having intercourse with her, or thinking that intercourse with an irrevocably divorced woman in the waiting period is permissible like intercourse with a revocable waiting-period woman. But there is consideration: because if a triple-irrevocably divorced woman is intercourse with by the husband under a mistaken belief, his mistake is in the act, and in that case lineage is not established even if he claims it, as the author has stated in the Book of Hudud. So how is lineage established here? The answer: it is conceded that a mistake in the act does not establish lineage even if claimed, if it is purely act-based, like intercourse with the slave-girl of his parents or the slave-girl of his wife; otherwise, like the triple-divorced woman or the one divorced for compensation, lineage is established by the claim, because the mistake in these is not purely act-based but also a mistake in the contract, so there is no contradiction between the two texts. In al-Nihayah: when the husband claims it, does it require the woman's confirmation? It said there are two narrations, and the most likely is that it is not required (Ramz al-Haqa'iq, 1/304). And 'minor girl' etc: meaning lineage is established for the child of a divorced minor girl, even if irrevocably, if she brings the child in less than nine months from the time of divorce. The meaning of minor girl (murahaqa) is a young girl of an age that coitus with her is possible, and she is at an age where she could have reached puberty, i.e., nine years old or more, and no signs of puberty have appeared on her. Only nine months is considered because three months is the duration of her waiting period and six months is the minimum duration of pregnancy. This is for the one consummated with. If he did not consummate with her, then if she brings it in less than six months from the time of divorce, his lineage is established due to conception in his marriage bed; if more, no, due to conception while she is a stranger. And the issue is restricted to her not confessing the expiry of the waiting period. If she confesses then brings a child in less than six months from the time of confession, his lineage is established; if six months or more, it is not established due to the expiry of the waiting period by her confession, and what she brings is not necessarily before it due to lack of certainty of her lie. And it is also restricted to her not claiming pregnancy; if she claims it, it is an acknowledgment that she has reached puberty, so her statement is accepted, and she becomes like an adult woman in terms of lineage establishment (Fath). 'For less than nine': meaning if she brings it in less [than nine] from the time he divorced her (Ayni). 'And if not, no': meaning if she does not give birth in less than nine months but gives birth in more than that, his lineage is not established, whether the divorce is irrevocable or revocable according to the two parties. Abu Yusuf said: it is established if she brings it up to two years, like an adult woman; and for a revocable divorce, his lineage is established up to twenty-seven months because he is considered to have intercourse at the end of the waiting period, which is three months, then she brings it at the maximum duration of pregnancy which is two years. The summary: pregnancy from a minor girl is doubtful, and the condition for the expiry of her waiting period by the passage of months is that she is not pregnant, and that is only known from her; as long as she has not confessed the expiry of her waiting period, it is possible she is pregnant from conception before the divorce in the case of irrevocable, and from conception during the waiting period in revocable. This amount of possibility is sufficient for the establishment of lineage, so it is attributed to him. And for them (the two shaykhs): we are certain of her minority =
Source pages p. 514

Commentary
This passage continues the discussion of lineage establishment with two special cases. First, an exception: lineage is established if the husband claims the child, provided there is a valid basis such as intercourse under mistaken belief (shubha) during the waiting period. The text clarifies the distinction between a shubha purely in the act (e.g., intercourse with a slave-girl) where lineage is not established even if claimed, and a shubha that includes a contractual aspect (e.g., triple-divorce or divorce for compensation) where lineage is established by claim. There is a discussion whether the woman's confirmation is needed; the preferred view is that it is not. Second, the case of a divorced minor girl (murahaqa) who has been consummated with: if she gives birth within nine months from the divorce (three months 'iddah plus six months minimum pregnancy), lineage is established. If more than nine months, it is not. For an unconsummated minor girl, the threshold is six months from divorce. Abu Yusuf disagrees, allowing up to two years for the minor girl in irrevocable divorce, and up to twenty-seven months in revocable divorce. The underlying principle is that pregnancy is doubtful in a minor, but as long as she has not confessed the expiry of her 'iddah, there is a possibility of conception during the marriage or waiting period, which suffices for lineage establishment.

Key Terms
المراهقة (al-murahaqah): A young girl of an age where sexual intercourse is possible but who has not yet reached puberty; described as a girl nine years or older without signs of puberty.
شبهة (shubhah): A mistaken belief or error that leads to a situation where the legal ruling may be mitigated; here, it refers to the husband's mistaken belief that intercourse during the waiting period was permissible.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the majority Hanafi view, within what period must a minor girl (murahaqa) give birth after an irrevocable divorce for the child's lineage to be established?
A) Six months
B) Nine months
C) Two years
D) Twenty-seven months

Key Takeaway
Lineage from a divorced minor wife is established only within nine months (three months 'iddah plus six months pregnancy), and the husband's claim can establish lineage only if based on a shubhah that includes a contractual element.

Proving Lineage from a Divorced Minor: The 9-Month Rule vs. the 2-Year Extension
Intra-Hanafi dispute on lineage timing for a divorced minor.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on proving lineage from a divorced minor and explain the difference between Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf's views.

Core Idea
Lineage from a divorced minor is proven only within 9 months; beyond that, only the husband's claim can establish it.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq addresses a subtle issue: when a minor wife is divorced, what time limit applies for establishing the husband's paternity if she later gives birth? The matn states a general rule of 9 months, but comments reveal an intra-Hanafi disagreement. Abu Hanifa holds firm to 9 months, while Abu Yusuf extends the window to 2 years. Understanding this ikhtilaf sharpens your ability to apply timing rules in family law.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core ruling
For a divorced minor (murahiqah) whose marriage was consummated, lineage is proven if birth occurs within 9 months of divorce. This is the general rule from the matn.
The 9 months consist of 3 months iddah plus 6 months minimum pregnancy.
2
Recognize the exception for husband's claim
The exception 'إلا أن يدعيه' allows lineage even beyond 9 months if the husband explicitly claims the child, because he assumes responsibility.
This exception is based on the husband's acceptance of paternity.
3
Distinguish consummated vs. non-consummated
If the marriage was not consummated, the window is 6 months (the minimum pregnancy period), since there is no iddah.
If birth occurs less than 6 months from divorce, lineage is proven; if exactly 6 months or more, it is not.
4
Identify the intra-Hanafi dispute
Abu Hanifa limits the period to 9 months for a minor. Abu Yusuf extends it to 2 years for any minor, and up to 27 months for a revocable divorce (3 months iddah + 2 years pregnancy).
The dispute hinges on whether a minor can be pregnant for longer than the typical maximum of 9 months.
5
Analyze the reasoning
Abu Hanifa argues that a minor's pregnancy is uncertain, but once iddah ends without evidence of pregnancy, the default is that the iddah is complete. Abu Yusuf argues that pregnancy can last up to 2 years, so the window should be extended.
The mufta bihi is Abu Hanifa's position (9 months).

The Book of Divorce. Chapter on Proving Lineage. Except if he claims it and the minor girl (who has reached an age where intercourse is possible) [gives birth] in less than nine months, otherwise no. i.e. the husband, because he has taken responsibility. If she was not consummated and she gave birth to a child in six months or more from the time of separation, the lineage is not proven, but if she gave birth in less than six months from the time of separation, it is proven. (Mukhtalas, Fath) ...
Source pages p. 514

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute. The base matn from Kanz al-Daqa'iq states a general rule: lineage from a divorced minor (murahiqa) is established only if she gives birth within nine months of the divorce, unless the husband claims the child. The commentary explains that the husband’s claim is an exception because he has accepted responsibility. For a non-consummated marriage, the period is six months. The main debate is between Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf regarding the maximum period for a minor. Abu Hanifa holds to nine months (or six for non-consummation) because the iddah is three months and minimum pregnancy is six months. Abu Yusuf extends the period to two years for a minor, reasoning that pregnancy can last that long, and for a revocable divorce he extends to 27 months. The commentary concludes that the pregnancy of a minor is uncertain, and as long as she has not admitted that her iddah has ended, it is possible she is pregnant, so lineage is established. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad argue that we are certain of her youth (which usually prevents pregnancy).

Key Terms
المراهقة (al-murahiqah): A girl who has reached the age where sexual intercourse is possible (typically 9 years or older) but may not have shown signs of puberty.
العلوق (al-ʿulūq): Conception; the moment when the sperm meets the ovum, used here to determine the earliest possible time of pregnancy.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a husband divorces his minor wife (murahiqah) and she gives birth 11 months later, what is the ruling on the child's lineage according to Abu Hanifa?
A) Lineage is established because she is a minor.
B) Lineage is not established because it is beyond 9 months.
C) Lineage is established only if the husband claims the child.
D) Lineage is established up to 27 months for a revocable divorce.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school establishes a strict 9-month limit for lineage from a divorced minor, but allows an exception if the husband claims the child.

Proving Lineage for a Widow and a Woman Who Admits Iddah Ended
Rulings on lineage from widows and women who admit iddah ended

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rules for establishing lineage in cases of a widow and a woman who admits her iddah ended, and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument.

Core Idea
Lineage from a widow is proven up to 2 years; a woman's admission of iddah end is trusted, so lineage is proven only within 6 months of her admission.

This lesson examines two situations: a widow giving birth after her husband's death, and a divorced woman who claims her iddah has finished. In both, the Hanafi school uses specific time limits to establish the child's lineage, balancing trust in the woman's statement with concern for certainty. The dispute with Imam al-Shafi'i on the second scenario highlights different priorities: the Hanafi school emphasizes the woman's reliability, while al-Shafi'i fears causing illegitimacy.

Guided Path
1
State the two scenarios
Identify the two distinct cases: (1) a widow observing iddah of death who gives birth, and (2) a woman who claims her iddah (from divorce or death) has ended and then gives birth.
2
Identify the Hanafi ruling for each
For the widow: lineage is established if birth occurs within 2 years of the husband's death. For the admitting woman: lineage is established if birth occurs within 6 months of her admission.
These time limits are based on the maximum pregnancy duration and the woman's trustworthiness.
3
Examine the Hanafi proofs
For the widow: the principle of caution (ihtiyat) in establishing lineage, and the medical fact that pregnancy can last up to two years. For the admitting woman: she is considered trustworthy (ameen) in her report, so her word is accepted unless contradicted by physical evidence.
Imam Zufar opposed the widow's 2-year rule, arguing for a fixed 10-month 10-day period, but his view is not adopted.
4
Present the Shafi'i objection
Imam al-Shafi'i argues that if a woman admits her iddah ended but gives birth after six months, the child should still be attributed to the husband, because she may have made a mistake and the default is legitimacy.
The Shafi'i school prioritizes avoiding attributing a child to zina over strict adherence to the woman's statement.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi response
The Hanafi school responds that her report is binding in legal matters; accepting it for the iddah but not for the child would be contradictory. Moreover, denying lineage does not necessarily imply zina, as she may have remarried.
The practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf) is that in the Hanafi school, the child is not attributed to the former husband, while in the Shafi'i school it is.

(فتح، عيني)
And [the case of] death in less than two years, and the woman who admits [the iddah has passed] in less than six months from the time of her admission, otherwise no. That is, the lineage of the child of the woman in iddah and the one who admits is established if her birth is denied [by the husband] with the testimony of two men or one man and two women...
Source pages p. 515

Commentary
This passage covers two separate but related rulings. First, for a widow (mu'taddah bil-mawt), lineage is proven if she gives birth within two years of her husband's death. Zufar argues for a shorter period (10 months and 10 days), but the Hanafi position uses the principle of caution (ihtiyat) in establishing lineage, and since pregnancy can last up to two years, the child is considered from the deceased if she does not admit the iddah ended. Second, for a woman who admits her iddah has ended but then gives birth, lineage is proven if birth occurs within six months of her admission, because her admission is taken as truthful (she is ameen). If birth occurs after six months, her admission is contradicted, so lineage is not proven. Imam al-Shafi'i disagrees, arguing that it is possible she made a mistake and the child should be attributed to the husband to avoid illegitimate. The Hanafi response is that she is trustworthy in her reports, so her word is accepted, even if it results in denying lineage, just as she is believed in ending iddah which prevents the husband's right to revoke.

Key Terms
المقرّة بمضيّها (al-muqirru bi-madiyyiha): A woman who voluntarily states that her iddah (waiting period) has come to an end.
معتدة الموت (mu'taddat al-mawt): A widow observing the iddah of death (4 months and 10 days).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A widow gives birth 18 months after her husband's death. According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on the child's lineage?
A) Lineage is not established because the iddah of death is only 4 months 10 days.
B) Lineage is established because birth occurred within 2 years.
C) Lineage is established only if she didn't admit the iddah ended.
D) Lineage is not established because it's beyond 9 months.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, lineage from a widow is established up to two years after the husband's death, while a woman's claim of iddah ending is trusted, limiting lineage to within six months of her claim.
