Minimum and Maximum Pregnancy Duration in Hanafi Fiqh
Hanafi ruling with Quranic proof and inter-madhhab comparison

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on pregnancy duration, derive the six-month minimum from the Quranic verses, and explain the evidence for the two-year maximum, distinguishing it from other schools.

Core Idea
The Hanafi school sets pregnancy at six months minimum and two years maximum, derived from Quranic arithmetic and the sunnah.

Determining the duration of pregnancy is not merely a medical question—it has profound legal consequences for lineage, inheritance, and iddah. The Hanafi school arrives at a precise ruling through a unique combination of two Quranic verses, while other schools rely on empirical reports. This lesson unpacks that derivation and the evidence for the maximum limit.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its scope
Note the Hanafi position: minimum 6 months, maximum 2 years. Understand that this ruling applies to establishing paternity and freeing of umm walad.
The ruling is factual but legally binding.
2
Derive the minimum from the Quran
Combine Surah al-Ahqaf 46:15 (total 30 months) and Surah Luqman 31:14 (weaning 24 months). Subtract: 30 - 24 = 6 months minimum pregnancy.
This is a direct qiyas between Quranic statements.
3
Examine the evidence for the maximum
The Hanafi school relies on the statement of Aisha (ra) that a child does not remain in the womb beyond two years, even for a fleeting moment. This is accepted as reliable transmitted knowledge.
Other schools cite historical anecdotes (e.g., al-Dahhak), but Hanafis reject them as unsubstantiated.
4
Contrast with other schools
Compare the Hanafi maximum (2 years) with Shafi'i (4 years), Maliki/Hanbali (5 or 7 years), and others (3-6 years). Understand that the core evidence differs: Hanafi relies on hadith, others on empirical stories.
The Hanafi position is the shortest maximum.
5
Apply the ruling to a practical scenario
Consider the case of a woman who marries, divorces, and is then repurchased. If she gives birth within 6 months of repurchase, the child belongs to the buyer; otherwise not.
This illustrates the six-month minimum as a legal threshold for paternity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وعن وأكثر مدة الحمل سنتان عندنا، وقال الشافعي: أربع سنين، وهو المشهور من مذهب مالك وأحمد، خمس سنين وعنه سبع سنين وهو قول ربيعة وعن الزهري ست سنين وعن الليث بن سعد: ثلاث سنين، مالك: = كتاب الطلاق ۵۱۷ باب ثبوت النسب وأقلها ستة أشهر ، فلو نكح أمة فطلقها فاشتراها فولدت لأقل من ستة أشهر منه أي أقل مدة الحمل بالاتفاق أي رجل لرجل آخر أي الأمة أي من وقت الشراء لزمه، وإلا لا، ومن قال لأمته إن كان في بطنك ولد فهو مني فشهدت امرأة أي فقالت ولدت بالولادة فهي أم ولده، قابلة مقبولة الشهادة وعن أبي عبيد : ليس لأقصاه وقت يوقف عليه، وتعلقوا في ذلك بحكايات لا يثبت الحكم بها، منها: ما روي أن الضحاك بقي في بطن أمه أربع سنين، فولدته أمه، وقد نبتت ثناياه وهو يضحك فسمي بذلك، والحجة عليهم قول عائشة لها : الولد لا يبقى في البطن أكثر من سنتين ولو بظل مغزل أي بقدر مكث ظله حين الدوران، وهذا تمثيل لغاية السرعة، فإن ظل المغزل حالة الدوران أسرع زوالاً من سائر الظلال، ويروى ولو بفلكة مغزل أي ولو بقدر دوران فلكة مغزل وهو محمول على السماع؛ لأنه لا يدرك بالرأي رمز الحقائق: ٣٠٦/١] (فتح) وأقلها ستة أشهر : بالإجماع، قال تعالى: ﴿وَحَمْلُهُ وَفِصَالُهُ ثَلاثُونَ شَهْرا﴾ (الأحقاف:١٥)، وقال: ﴿وَفِصَالُهُ فِي عَامَيْنِ (لقمان:١٤)، فيبقى للحمل ستة أشهر، روي هذا عن علي وابن عباس . رمز الحقائق: ٣٠٦/١] (فتح)
And regarding the maximum duration of pregnancy: two years according to us. Al-Shafi'i said: four years. The well-known view of Malik and Ahmad: five years, and from him seven years, which is the view of Rabi'a. From al-Zuhri: six years. From al-Layth ibn Sa'd: three years. Malik: = ... The minimum is six months. So if he married a slave woman, divorced her, then bought her, and she gave birth in less than six months from that [time], the child belongs to him, otherwise not. And whoever says to his slave woman: 'If there is a child in your womb, it is from me,' and one woman testified, i.e., said she gave birth, then she is umm walad... The proof against them is the saying of Aisha: The child does not remain in the womb more than two years, even if by the shadow of a spindle... And the minimum is six months by consensus. Allah said: 'And his carrying and his weaning is thirty months' and 'And his weaning is in two years,' so six months remain for pregnancy.
Source pages p. 517

Commentary
This passage presents the Hanafi position on the duration of pregnancy. It states that according to the Hanafi school, the maximum period of pregnancy is two years, while other schools differ: Shafi'i holds four years; Maliki and Hanbali generally five or seven years; other opinions exist. The text then moves to the minimum, which is six months by consensus. It provides the Quranic evidence: surah al-Ahqaf verse 15 states that the total period of pregnancy and weaning is thirty months, and surah Luqman verse 14 states that weaning is two years (twenty-four months). Thus, thirty minus twenty-four leaves six months as the minimum duration of pregnancy. This is attributed to Ali and Ibn Abbas. The text also mentions an example: if a man marries a slave woman, divorces her, then purchases her, and she gives birth within six months of the purchase, the child's lineage is established to the buyer. This illustrates the application of the six-month minimum. Additionally, it discusses the story of al-Dahhak, who reportedly remained in his mother's womb for four years, but dismisses such anecdotes as unreliable evidence. The definitive proof is the saying of Aisha that the fetus does not stay beyond two years, which is transmitted knowledge.

Key Terms
مدة الحمل (muddah al-haml): The duration a fetus can be carried in the womb; legally relevant for lineage, iddah, and inheritance.
فصال (fisal): Weaning of a child; Quranically set at two years.
أم ولد (umm walad): A slave woman who bears a child from her master; she becomes free upon his death.
ظل مغزل (zill maghzil): The shadow of a spindle—a metaphor for an extremely short period of time.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the maximum duration of pregnancy?
A) Six months
B) Two years
C) Four years
D) Seven years

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school sets pregnancy at a minimum of six months and a maximum of two years, with the minimum derived from the Quran and the maximum from the sunnah.

Talaq — Divorce

Automatic Lineage When Buying a Divorced Slave Wife: The Six-Month Rule
First half of a longer passage: six-month rule from purchase.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which a man automatically establishes lineage to a child born to his divorced slave wife within six months of purchase.

Core Idea
If birth occurs within six months of purchase, lineage is automatic—conception is presumed during the marriage iddah.

This lesson unpacks a fiqh scenario: a man marries a slave woman, divorces her after consummation (either revocably or irrevocably), then purchases her. If she gives birth within six months of the purchase, the child's lineage is established to him without any need for a claim. The underlying legal presumption rests on the minimum pregnancy period of six months and the continuity of the iddah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what action is being ruled upon: a man buying his divorced slave wife who gives birth. The ruling is that the child's lineage is binding upon the buyer without any claim.
The divorce must be after consummation (dakhul).
2
List the conditions for automatic paternity
Three conditions: (1) divorce after consummation, (2) purchase after divorce, (3) birth within six months from the time of purchase.
If any condition is missing, lineage is not automatic.
3
Understand the legal reasoning (ta'lil)
Because the divorce triggers an iddah, and purchase does not cancel the iddah for others. The conception must have occurred during the iddah (within the marriage) if birth is less than six months after purchase.
This is based on the Hanafi rule that the minimum pregnancy is six months.
4
Apply to a real scenario
Example: A man buys his divorced slave wife on Jan 1. She gives birth on May 15 (less than 6 months). The child is his without claim. If she gives birth on July 15 (more than 6 months), lineage requires his claim.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فطلقها: بعد الدخول بائناً أو رجعياً. (ط،ع) لزمه: أي نسب الولد بلا دعوة؛ لأنه ولد المعتدة لتقدم العلوق على الشراء فيلزمه سواء أقر به أو نفاه. (ط،ع) وإلا لا: هذا تفريع على قوله : أقل مدة الحمل ستة أشهر أي من تزوج أمة غيره فطلقها طلاقاً واحداً بائناً ثم اشتراها فولدت لأقل من ستة أشهر من وقت الشراء لزمه النسب أي يثبت نسبه منه بلا دعوة؛ لأنه ولد المعتدة لتقدم العلوق على الشراء؛ لأنه لما طلقها وجبت عليها العدة ثم بالشراء لم تبطل العدة في حق غيره، وإن بطلت بالنسبة إليه لحلها له بملك اليمين وإن لم تلد لأقل من ستة أشهر بل ولدت لستة أو لأكثر منها لا يثبت نسبه منه إلا أن يدعيه أنه ولد المملوكة لا المعتدة لتأخر العلوق عن الشراء، فلا يلزمه إلا بالدعوة، هذا إذا كان الطلاق بعد الدخول واحداً بائناً أو خلعاً أو رجعياً؛ إذ لو كان قبل الدخول بها لا يلزمه الولد إلا أن تلد لأقل من ستة أشهر مذ طلقها؛ لأن العلوق حدث في حال قيام النكاح. وإن طلقها ثنتين حتى حرمت عليه حرمة غليظة يثبت النسب إلى سنتين من وقت الطلاق؛ لأنه لا يمكن إضافة العلوق إلى ما بعد الشراء للحرمة الغليظة فيضاف إلى أبعد الأوقات، وهو ما قبل الطلاق حملاً لأمرها على الصلاح، واعلم أن الطلاق ليس بقيد بل إذا اشترى زوجته قبل أن يطلقها فهو ذلك في جميع ما ذكرنا من الأحكام؛ لأن النكاح يفسد بالشراء، وتكون معتدة إن كان بعد الدخول فيكون ما ولدته قبل ستة أشهر ولد المنكوحة، وبعده ولد المملوكة وكذلك الشراء ليس بقيد، بل المراد أنها دخلت في ملكه بأي سبب كونه قبل الإقرار بانقضاء عدتها. (مستخلص عيني، فتح) فهي: أي الأمة تصير أم ولده إجماعاً إذا ولدته لأقل من . ستة أشهر من وقت الإقرار، ولو لأكثر لا. (ط)
He divorced her: after consummation, irrevocably or revocably. (Ta, A) It is binding: i.e., the child's lineage is established without claim, because it is the child of the woman in iddah, since the conception preceded the purchase, so it is binding whether he acknowledges or denies it. (Ta, A) Otherwise no: This is a branch on his saying: the minimum pregnancy is six months. Meaning: whoever married another's slave woman, divorced her with a single irrevocable divorce, then bought her, and she gave birth in less than six months from the time of purchase, the lineage is binding, i.e., his lineage is established from him without claim... And if he divorces her twice, so that it becomes a severe prohibition, the lineage is established up to two years from the time of divorce... So she: i.e., the slave woman becomes umm walad by consensus if she gives birth in less than six months from the time of acknowledgment, but not if more.
Source pages p. 518

Commentary
This passage expands on the application of the six-month minimum pregnancy rule in the context of a man who marries a slave woman, divorces her, and then purchases her. It details the conditions under which the child's lineage is established to the purchaser. If the divorce occurred after consummation (either irrevocably or revocably), and she gives birth within six months of the purchase, the child is attributed to the buyer without his claiming it, because the conception must have occurred during the marriage (the iddah period). This holds even if the buyer denies paternity. If she gives birth after six months from purchase, the child is not automatically his; he must claim it, as the conception likely occurred after purchase, making the child a slave. The text also covers cases where the divorce was before consummation, where the child is only attributed if born within six months from the divorce. Additionally, if the man divorces her with two divorces (making her severely prohibited), the lineage can be established up to two years from the divorce, as the severe prohibition prevents adding conception to after purchase. The passage concludes that the slave woman becomes umm walad (mother of the master's child) by consensus if she gives birth within six months of his acknowledgment of paternity.

Key Terms
معتدة (mu'taddah): A woman in her waiting period (iddah) after divorce or death; here specifically the divorced slave woman.
علوق ('uluq): Conception; the moment the fetus is formed; used to determine timing of lineage.
أم ولد (umm walad): A slave woman who bears a child from her master; she becomes free upon his death and the child is free.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Automatically established without claim
B) Not established unless the buyer claims
C) The child is free but not attributed to the buyer
D) The child belongs to the seller

Key Takeaway
If a divorced slave wife gives birth within six months of purchase, the child is automatically attributed to the buyer without any claim.

Extended Scenarios: Pre-Consummation, Severe Prohibition, and Umm Walad
Second half of passage: pre-consummation, two divorces, and umm walad.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the lineage rules for cases of divorce before consummation, two divorces (severe prohibition), and when the woman becomes umm walad.

Core Idea
For severe prohibition (two divorces), lineage extends up to two years; for pre-consummation, only within six months of divorce; umm walad status follows the child's recognition.

The source text continues with additional scenarios that refine the six-month rule. If divorce occurred before consummation, the child only binds the buyer if born within six months of the divorce. If two divorces have been pronounced (severe prohibition), lineage can be established up to two years from the divorce because the conception cannot be attributed to the purchase period due to the prohibition. Finally, the text notes that a slave woman becomes umm walad by consensus if she gives birth within six months of the master's acknowledgment.

Guided Path
1
Identify the special cases
Three special cases: (1) divorce before consummation, (2) two divorces (severe prohibition), (3) umm walad via acknowledgment within six months.
2
Apply the time frames
For case (1): birth within 6 months from divorce. For case (2): birth within 2 years from divorce. For case (3): birth within 6 months from acknowledgment.
These are extensions of the basic pregnancy presumption.
3
Understand the rationale for the two-year rule
Because severe prohibition prevents adding conception after purchase; the lineage is attributed to the farthest possible time (two years) to presume conception during the marriage.
This is based on the principle of carrying the woman's case on goodness (haml al-amr 'ala al-salah).
4
Recognize the consensus on umm walad
If the woman gives birth within six months of the master's acknowledgment, she becomes umm walad by consensus; after six months, she does not.
This shows the consistency of the six-month rule across different contexts.

Minimum and Maximum Duration of Pregnancy
Establishes minimum and maximum pregnancy duration with Quranic proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the minimum and maximum duration of pregnancy and derive it from the Quranic verses and hadith.

Core Idea
Minimum pregnancy is six months, maximum two years — derived from combining two Quranic verses.

This lesson examines a key ruling in Hanafi fiqh: the minimum and maximum duration of pregnancy. This ruling has direct implications for lineage, inheritance, and the iddah period. The Hanafi school establishes these durations not by medical opinion but by clear textual proofs from the Quran and hadith, rejecting anecdotal stories that suggest longer periods.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi ruling on minimum and maximum pregnancy
Identify what the school holds: minimum six months, maximum two years.
This is a factual legal determination, not a hukm taklifi.
2
Locate the Quranic proof for the minimum
Examine the two verses: Surah al-Ahqaf (46:15) and Surah Luqman (31:14). The first states gestation and weaning total thirty months; the second states weaning alone is twenty-four months.
The combination yields six months for gestation.
3
Explain the mathematical derivation
Subtract 24 months (weaning) from 30 months (gestation + weaning) to get 6 months minimum gestation.
This derivation is attributed to Ali and Ibn Abbas.
4
Identify the proof for the maximum
The hadith of Aisha (r.a.) states that a child does not remain in the womb for more than two years, even by the shadow of a spindle.
This is a transmitted proof (samā' ) that cannot be known by opinion.
5
Note the opposition and Hanafi response
Some scholars (e.g., Abu Ubayd) argued for no fixed maximum, citing stories like al-Dahhak born after four years. The Hanafi response: such stories are not legally binding; the hadith of Aisha is authoritative.
The Hanafi position is based on strong textual evidence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأقلها ستة أشهر : بالإجماع، قال تعالى: ﴿وَحَمْلُهُ وَفِصَالُهُ ثَلاثُونَ شَهْرًا﴾ (الأحقاف:١٥)، وقال: ﴿وَفِصَالُهُ فِي عَامَيْنِ﴾ (لقمان:١٤)، فيبقى للحمل ستة أشهر، روي هذا عن علي وابن عباس. وعن أبي عبيد : ليس لأقصاه وقت يوقف عليه، وتعلقوا في ذلك بحكايات لا يثبت الحكم بها، منها: ما روي أن الضحاك بقي في بطن أمه أربع سنين، فولدته أمه، وقد نبتت ثناياه وهو يضحك فسمي بذلك، والحجة عليهم قول عائشة لها : الولد لا يبقى في البطن أكثر من سنتين ولو بظل مغزل أي بقدر مكث ظله حين الدوران، وهذا تمثيل لغاية السرعة، فإن ظل المغزل حالة الدوران أسرع زوالاً من سائر الظلال، ويروى ولو بفلكة مغزل أي ولو بقدر دوران فلكة مغزل وهو محمول على السماع؛ لأنه لا يدرك بالرأي
And its minimum is six months by consensus. Allah Almighty said: 'And his gestation and weaning is thirty months' (al-Ahqaf:15), and He said: 'And his weaning is in two years' (Luqman:14), so for pregnancy remains six months. This is narrated from Ali and Ibn Abbas. And from Abu Ubayd: There is no time limit for its maximum that can be determined. And they relied in that on stories that cannot establish a ruling. Among them: what is narrated that al-Dahhak remained in his mother's womb for four years, then his mother gave birth to him while his incisors had grown and he was laughing, so he was named accordingly. And the proof against them is the saying of Aisha: The child does not remain in the womb for more than two years, even by the shadow of a spindle, meaning the duration of the staying of its shadow when it rotates. This is a metaphor for extreme speed, for the shadow of a spindle during rotation disappears faster than other shadows. And it is narrated 'even by the whorl of a spindle', meaning even by the duration of the rotation of a spindle's whorl. And it is interpreted as based on hearsay, because it cannot be perceived by opinion.
Source pages p. 518

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof establishing the minimum and maximum duration of pregnancy. The matn states that the minimum duration is six months by consensus (ijma). The proof is derived from two Quranic verses: Surah al-Ahqaf 46:15 states that the total period of gestation and weaning is thirty months, and Surah Luqman 31:14 states that weaning is in two years (twenty-four months). Subtracting twenty-four from thirty leaves six months as the minimum pregnancy period. This interpretation is attributed to Ali ibn Abi Talib and Ibn Abbas. As for the maximum duration, the Hanafi school holds that there is no fixed limit that can be determined by opinion, but it is established by transmitted reports (samā‘). The text mentions a story of al-Dahhak who was born after four years, but such stories are not legally binding proofs. The proof for the two-year maximum is the hadith of Aisha that a child does not remain in the womb for more than two years, even for the duration of a spindle's shadow—a metaphor for a very short time. This is considered a transmitted proof (samā‘) because it cannot be known by reason alone.

Key Terms
علوق (ʿulūq): The beginning of pregnancy, conception.
فصال (fiṣāl): Weaning; stopping breastfeeding.
حمل (ḥaml): Pregnancy; gestation period.
فلكة مغزل (falakat maghzal): Whorl of a spindle, used in the hadith as a metaphor for the shortest possible time.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the maximum duration of pregnancy according to the Hanafi school?
A) Two years
B) Four years
C) No fixed maximum
D) One year

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school determines the minimum pregnancy as six months and maximum as two years, derived from Quranic verses and the hadith of Aisha.

10 min
Lineage of Child Born to Divorced and Repurchased Amah
Ruling with rational proof based on minimum pregnancy period

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state when the lineage of a child born to a divorced and then purchased amah is automatically established and when it requires a claim.

Core Idea
Birth within six months of purchase establishes lineage automatically; otherwise, paternity must be claimed.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq addresses a nuanced scenario: a man marries another's slave woman, divorces her, and later purchases her. The timing of the birth relative to the purchase determines whether the child's lineage is automatically binding. The ruling hinges on the minimum pregnancy period of six months and the legal status of the woman (whether she is in iddah or a mere slave). Understanding this rule helps prevent confusion about paternity claims in similar ownership situations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Core Scenario
Begin by recognizing the sequence: marriage to another's amah, divorce (after consummation), then purchase of that amah. The ruling focuses on the child born after purchase.
Divorce can be single ba'in, khul', or raj'i; also two talaq cases.
2
Distinguish the Timing of Birth
Check whether the birth occurs within less than six months from the time of purchase, or at six months or more. This is the key dividing line.
Six months is the minimum pregnancy duration in Hanafi fiqh.
3
Apply the Rule for Automatic Lineage
If the birth is within less than six months, lineage is binding automatically (without a claim) because the conception must have occurred during the woman's iddah period before she was purchased.
The child is considered a child of the woman in iddah (walad al-mu'tadda).
4
Apply the Rule for Non-Automatic Lineage
If the birth is at six months or more, lineage is not established unless the man explicitly claims paternity, because conception likely occurred after purchase (making the child a child of the slave woman).
The man may still claim paternity if he wishes.
5
Extend to Variations in Divorce and Ownership
Note that the same logic applies if the divorce was before consummation, or if he purchased his wife without divorcing first, or if the divorce was two talaq (extending the window to two years). The principle remains consistent: the iddah period and the minimum pregnancy term govern.
Also applies when the woman enters his possession by any means before her iddah expires.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فلو نكح أمة فطلقها فاشتراها فولدت لأقل من ستة أشهر منه لزمه، وإلا لا. (ط) لزمه: أي نسب الولد بلا دعوة؛ لأنه ولد المعتدة لتقدم العلوق على الشراء فيلزمه سواء أقر به أو نفاه. (ط،ع) وإلا لا: هذا تفريع على قوله : أقل مدة الحمل ستة أشهر أي من تزوج أمة غيره فطلقها طلاقاً واحداً بائناً ثم اشتراها فولدت لأقل من ستة أشهر من وقت الشراء لزمه النسب أي يثبت نسبه منه بلا دعوة؛ لأنه ولد المعتدة لتقدم العلوق على الشراء؛ لأنه لما طلقها وجبت عليها العدة ثم بالشراء لم تبطل العدة في حق غيره، وإن بطلت بالنسبة إليه لحلها له بملك اليمين وإن لم تلد لأقل من ستة أشهر بل ولدت لستة أو لأكثر منها لا يثبت نسبه منه إلا أن يدعيه أنه ولد المملوكة لا المعتدة لتأخر العلوق عن الشراء، فلا يلزمه إلا بالدعوة، هذا إذا كان الطلاق بعد الدخول واحداً بائناً أو خلعاً أو رجعياً؛ إذ لو كان قبل الدخول بها لا يلزمه الولد إلا أن تلد لأقل من ستة أشهر مذ طلقها؛ لأن العلوق حدث في حال قيام النكاح. وإن طلقها ثنتين حتى حرمت عليه حرمة غليظة يثبت النسب إلى سنتين من وقت الطلاق؛ لأنه لا يمكن إضافة العلوق إلى ما بعد الشراء للحرمة الغليظة فيضاف إلى أبعد الأوقات، وهو ما قبل الطلاق حملاً لأمرها على الصلاح، واعلم أن الطلاق ليس بقيد بل إذا اشترى زوجته قبل أن يطلقها فهو ذلك في جميع ما ذكرنا من الأحكام؛ لأن النكاح يفسد بالشراء، وتكون معتدة إن كان بعد الدخول فيكون ما ولدته قبل ستة أشهر ولد المنكوحة، وبعده ولد المملوكة وكذلك الشراء ليس بقيد، بل المراد أنها دخلت في ملكه بأي سبب كونه قبل الإقرار بانقضاء عدتها.
So if he married an amah, then divorced her, then bought her, and she gave birth within less than six months from him (i.e., from the time of purchase), it is binding upon him, otherwise not. (T) 'Binding' means the lineage of the child is established without a claim (of paternity), because it is a child of the woman in iddah, due to the conception preceding the purchase, so it is binding whether he acknowledges or denies it. (T, A) 'Otherwise not' is a branching from his statement: the minimum duration of pregnancy is six months. That is: whoever married another's amah and divorced her with a single irrevocable divorce, then bought her, and she gave birth within less than six months from the time of purchase, the lineage is binding upon him, i.e., his paternity is established without a claim, because it is the child of the woman in iddah, due to the conception preceding the purchase. Because when he divorced her, the iddah became obligatory, then by the purchase the iddah did not become void with respect to others, even if it became void with respect to him because she becomes permissible to him by right of ownership. And if she did not give birth within less than six months, but gave birth at six months or more, his paternity is not established unless he claims it, because it is the child of the slave woman, not of the woman in iddah, due to the conception being after the purchase. So it is not binding except by his claim. This applies if the divorce was after consummation, whether a single irrevocable divorce, or khul', or revocable. But if the divorce was before consummation, the child is not binding upon him unless she gives birth within less than six months from the time he divorced her, because the conception occurred while the marriage was still valid. And if he divorced her with two divorces such that she becomes prohibited with a severe prohibition, the lineage is established up to two years from the time of divorce, because it is impossible to attribute the conception to after the purchase due to the severe prohibition, so it is attributed to the farthest time, which is before the divorce, assuming her situation to be sound. And know that divorce is not a stipulation; rather if he purchases his wife before divorcing her, the same applies in all the rulings we have mentioned, because marriage is invalidated by purchase, and she becomes in iddah if it was after consummation. So what she gives birth to before six months is a child of the married woman (nikah), and after that it is a child of the slave woman. Similarly, purchase is not a stipulation; rather the meaning is that she came into his possession by any means, provided that it is before acknowledging the expiry of her iddah.
Source pages p. 518

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with explanation covering the case of a man who marries a slave woman (amah) belonging to someone else, then divorces her, then buys her, and she gives birth. The key principle is the minimum pregnancy period of six months. If the child is born within six months of the purchase, the lineage from the man is established automatically without any need for him to claim paternity, because the conception must have occurred during the iddah period after divorce, making the child a child of the woman in iddah ('ulūq al-muʿtadda). If the child is born after six months, lineage is not established unless the man explicitly claims the child, because then it is likely a child conceived after purchase, i.e., a child of the slave woman (walad al-mamlūka). The ruling differs based on the type of divorce: if the divorce is after consummation, the above applies; if before consummation, the child is only binding if born within six months of the divorce, because conception could only have occurred during the valid marriage. If the divorce was two divorces (making her severely prohibited), the child's lineage is extended up to two years from the divorce, because the severe prohibition prevents attributing conception to after purchase. The commentator also clarifies that both divorce and purchase are not the only triggers; any way the woman enters the man's ownership, the same principle applies as long as the iddah has not been acknowledged to have ended.

Key Terms
المعتدة (al-muʿtadda): A woman undergoing iddah (waiting period) after divorce.
العلوق (al-ʿulūq): Conception; the beginning of pregnancy.
بائن (bāʾin): Irrevocable divorce (where the husband cannot take back the wife without a new marriage).
رجعي (rajʿī): Revocable divorce (where the husband can take back the wife during iddah without new marriage).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Automatically, because six months is the minimum pregnancy period
B) Only by the man's claim, because birth at six months is not 'less than six months'
C) Automatically, because she was in iddah at purchase
D) Not established at all

Key Takeaway
The six-month window from purchase is the decisive factor: birth within that period automatically establishes lineage; otherwise, a claim is required.

Paternity Declaration for Amah and Midwife Testimony
Ruling on conditions for umm walad status

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which a man's declaration of paternity makes his amah an umm walad and explain the role of the midwife's testimony.

Core Idea
A declaration alone does not make an umm walad; birth within six months is required.

This passage addresses a specific scenario in Hanafi fiqh: a man says to his amah, 'If there is a child in your womb, it is from me.' A midwife then testifies that she gave birth. The ruling clarifies when this makes the amah an umm walad. The key condition is the time between the declaration and the birth, demonstrating the Hanafi emphasis on certainty and minimal pregnancy periods.

Guided Path
1
Isolate the declaration and its legal effect
Identify the man's statement as a conditional declaration of paternity (iqrar). The intended legal effect is that the amah becomes an umm walad, a status with significant consequences (e.g., freedom upon master's death).
2
Apply the temporal condition
Note that the effect depends on the birth occurring within less than six months from the declaration. This six-month period corresponds to the minimum pregnancy duration in Hanafi law.
If birth occurs at exactly six months or more, the condition fails.
3
Assess the midwife's testimony
The midwife's testimony is admissible to confirm the birth. The text indicates that a reliable midwife (qābila maqbūla al-shahāda) is acceptable. Her testimony is necessary but does not override the time condition.
The testimony may come from any woman present at birth, not necessarily a midwife, as long as she is reliable.
4
Conclude the status
If both conditions are met (birth within six months and acceptable testimony), the amah becomes an umm walad by consensus. Otherwise, she does not.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن قال لأمته إن كان في بطنك ولد فهو مني فشهدت امرأة أي فقالت ولدت بالولادة فهي أم ولده، قابلة مقبولة الشهادة فهي: أي الأمة تصير أم ولده إجماعاً إذا ولدته لأقل من ستة أشهر من وقت الإقرار، ولو لأكثر لا. (ط) من كان، ولابد
And if a man says to his amah, 'If there is a child in your womb, it is from me,' then a woman testifies, i.e., she says she gave birth, then she becomes an umm walad. [If the midwife is] acceptable, her testimony is accepted. So she (the amah) becomes his umm walad by consensus if she gives birth within less than six months from the time of the acknowledgment, but if more, then no. (T) Whoever is, and it is necessary?
Source pages p. 518

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement about the effect of a man's declaration of paternity regarding his amah's unborn child. If he says to his amah, 'If what is in your womb is a child, it is from me,' and a midwife (or another woman) testifies that she gave birth, then the amah becomes an umm walad (mother of a child) by consensus, provided the birth occurs within less than six months from the time of his declaration (iqrār). This six-month condition is the same as the minimum pregnancy period. If she gives birth after six months or more, she does not become an umm walad. The midwife's testimony is accepted if she is a reliable witness (qābila maqbūla al-shahāda). The phrase 'من كان، ولابد' might be an incomplete note; the meaning is that the ruling applies regardless of who the midwife is, as long as her testimony is accepted.

Key Terms
أم ولد (umm walad): A slave woman who has borne a child to her master, with specific legal status (she becomes free upon his death).
قابلة (qābila): A midwife; a woman who assists in childbirth.
إقرار (iqrar): Acknowledgment or declaration; here, the master's statement claiming paternity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) When the child is born, regardless of time

D) Only if a midwife testifies and the child is born within six months

Key Takeaway
A man's declaration of paternity for his amah's child makes her an umm walad only if the child is born within six months of the declaration, with a midwife's testimony confirming the birth.

Inheritance When a Man Claims a Son and Mother Claims Marriage
Ruling on inheritance of woman claiming marriage

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which a woman claiming to be the wife inherits when a man acknowledges a boy as his son, and explain the Hanafi use of istihsan over qiyas in this case.

Core Idea
The Hanafi prefer istihsan over qiyas: acknowledging a child implies a valid marriage if the mother is free, Muslim, and known as the mother.

This passage examines a complex inheritance scenario where a man acknowledges a boy as his son but dies. The mother claims to be the wife and seeks inheritance. The Hanafi school uses istihsan to presume a valid marriage, setting aside the strict analogy that acknowledgment of a child does not imply marriage. The conditions for this presumption and the three ranks of lineage establishment are explained.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
A man says of a boy, 'He is my son,' then dies. The mother claims 'I am his wife and he is my son from him.'
Both claim inheritance: the son inherits as a child, the mother claims as a wife.
2
List the conditions for the mother's inheritance by istihsan
The mother inherits only if she is known to be originally free, Muslim, and known to be the mother of the boy. If any condition is missing (e.g., her freedom is unknown), she does not inherit.
These conditions are not required for the son's inheritance; his lineage is established by the man's claim.
3
Understand the qiyas argument
By strict analogy (qiyas), acknowledging the child does not imply acknowledging marriage, because lineage can also be established through invalid marriage, shubha, or umm walad. Therefore, she should not inherit.
Qiyas would deny her inheritance entirely.
4
Understand the istihsan override
Istihsan (juristic preference) overrides qiyas here because the case is defined by the three conditions. When a woman is known to be free, Muslim, and the mother, a valid marriage is the default assumption for lineage. Hence, his acknowledgment of the child implies a valid marriage, and she inherits.
This is a distinctive Hanafi use of istihsan to favor certainty and public interest.
5
Note the three ranks of lineage establishment
The appendix lists three ranks: (1) marriage – lineage established without claim, not negated by mere denial; (2) umm walad – lineage established without claim but negated by denial; (3) slave woman – lineage requires a claim (Hanafi view, contrary to Shafi'i).
This clarifies the different evidentiary standards for different relationships.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن قال لغلام هو ابني، ومات فقالت أمّه أنا امرأته وهو ابنه مني يرثانه، وإن جهلت حرّيتُها ، فقال وارثه أنت أمّ ولد أبي فلا ميراث لها. فهي أم ولده أي ثبت نسب الولد منه؛ لأن سبب ثبوت النسب وهو الدعوة قد وجد من المولى بقوله: فهو مني وإنما الحاجة إلى تعيين الولد وهو يثبت بشهادة القابلة اتفاقاً، هذا إذا ولدته لأقل من ستة أشهر من وقت قال ذلك؛ للتيقن لوجوده في ذلك الوقت، وإن ولدته لأكثر منها لا يلزمه لاحتمال العلوق بعده . أمه المعروفة بحرية الأصل والإسلام وبأنها أم الغلام (ط) يرثانه والقياس أن لا يكون لها الإرث؛ لأن النسب يثبت بالنكاح الفاسد وبالوطء بشبهة وبأمومية الولد فلا يكون الإقرار بالولد إقراراً بالزوجية لها، وجه الاستحسان: أن المسألة مفروضة فيما إذا كانت معروفة بالحرية والإسلام وبكونها أم الغلام والنكاح الصحيح هو المتعين للنسب، فعند إقراره بالبنوة يحمل عليه ما لم يظهر خلافه . فقال وارثه: قول الوارث ليس بقيد بل الجهل بالحرية كاف في منع إرثها سواء قال الوارث ذلك أم لا أو كان صغيراً، وقوله فلا ميراث لها؛ لأن الحرية الثابتة بظاهر الحال باعتبار الدار تصلح لدفع الرق، ولا تصلح لاستحقاق الإرث كاستصحاب الحال. وعلى هذا لو قال الوارث إنها كانت نصرانية وقت موت أبي ولم يعلم إسلامها فيه، أو قال: كانت زوجة له وهي أمة ينبغي أن لا ترث؛ لما قلنا وقالوا: لها مهر المثل في مسألة الكتابية؛ لأن الوارث أقر بالدخول عليها، ولم يثبت كونها أم ولد. تتمة: لثبوت النسب ثلاث مراتب إحداها النكاح، والحكم فيه أنه يثبت بلا دعوة ولا ينتفي بمجرد النفي، الثانية: أم الولد، والحكم فيها أن يثبت النسب من غير دعوة وينتفي بمجرد النفي، الثالثة: الأمة إذا جاءت بولد لا يثبت النسب بدون الدعوة عندنا خلافاً للشافعي.
And if a man says of a boy, 'He is my son,' and dies, and his mother says, 'I am his wife and he is my son from him,' they both inherit. But if her freedom is unknown, and the heir says, 'You are the umm walad of my father,' then she has no inheritance. So she is his umm walad, meaning the lineage of the child is established from him because the cause of establishing lineage, which is the claim, has occurred from the master by his saying 'he is from me,' and the only need is to identify the child, and that is established by the testimony of the midwife by agreement. This is if she gave birth within less than six months from the time he said that, due to certainty of his existence at that time; but if she gave birth after more than that, it is not binding upon him due to the possibility of conception after it. And his mother, known to be originally free and Muslim and that she is the mother of the boy, (T) they both inherit. And by analogy (qiyas), she should not have inheritance, because lineage is established by an invalid marriage, by intercourse with a shubha, and by motherhood of the child, so acknowledging the child is not an acknowledgment of marriage to her. The basis of istihsan is that the case is assumed when she is known to be free and Muslim and that she is the mother of the boy, and a valid marriage is the default for lineage. So when he acknowledges the son, it is interpreted as such unless the contrary appears. Then the heir said: The statement of the heir is not a stipulation; rather, ignorance of her freedom is sufficient to prevent her inheritance, whether the heir says that or not, even if he is a minor. And his statement, 'so she has no inheritance' because freedom established by the apparent situation based on the abode is sufficient to repel slavery, but it is not sufficient to entitle inheritance, like the principle of istishab al-hal. And based on this, if the heir says she was Christian at the time of his father's death and he does not know her Islam, or he says she was his wife but she was a slave, then she should not inherit, for what we have said. And they said: she gets the dower of the like in the case of the Christian woman, because the heir acknowledged that he had intercourse with her, and it is not established that she is an umm walad. Appendix: For the establishment of lineage there are three ranks: First, marriage; its ruling is that it is established without a claim and is not negated merely by denial. Second, umm walad; its ruling is that lineage is established without a claim but is negated merely by denial. Third, the slave woman if she comes with a child; lineage is not established without a claim, according to us, contrary to al-Shafi'i.
Source pages p. 519

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof covering a complex inheritance case. A man says of a boy, 'He is my son,' then dies. The mother claims to be his wife, and they both should inherit. However, if her freedom is unknown, and the legal heir (e.g., the man's other relative) says she is simply the umm walad of the deceased father, then she does not inherit. The text then explains the conditions: the boy's lineage is established by the man's claim (da‘wa) and the midwife's testimony, provided the birth occurs within six months of the claim. The mother inherits only if she is known to be originally free and Muslim, and known to be the mother of the boy. By qiyas, acknowledging the child does not imply acknowledging marriage, so she should not inherit. However, istihsan prevails: because she is known to be free and Muslim and the mother, a valid marriage is presumed, so she inherits. If her freedom or Islam is unknown, she does not inherit. The commentator also notes that the heir's statement is not a condition; ignorance of her freedom alone prevents inheritance. The appendix lists three ranks of lineage establishment: (1) marriage: lineage established automatically and only denied by li‘an; (2) umm walad: established automatically but can be denied simply by denial; (3) slave woman: lineage requires a claim, unlike the Shafi‘i school.

Key Terms
أم ولد (umm walad): A slave woman who has borne a child to her master; she becomes free upon his death and her child is free and legitimate.
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference; setting aside qiyas for a stronger proof or public interest.
دعوة (da‘wa): Claim of paternity; explicit acknowledgment by the father.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Yes, because the boy inherits
B) No, because ignorance of freedom prevents inheritance
C) Yes, if she is Muslim
D) No, because she is a slave

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, acknowledging a child does not automatically establish marriage; inheritance of the mother requires that she be known as free, Muslim, and the boy's mother, based on istihsan.

The Mother's Right to Custody in Hanafi Law
Establishes the mother's priority and conditions for custody.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which a mother retains the right of custody (hadanah) and explain the legal effect of marriage to a non-mahram.

Core Idea
The mother is the primary custodian unless she marries a non-mahram; then her right is forfeited but returns upon separation.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq establishes the foundational principle of custody: the mother is the most entitled to the child, before and after divorce. This lesson unpacks the conditions that preserve or forfeit her right, the proof from the Prophet's hadith, and the ancillary ruling on payment for custody.

Guided Path
1
Identify the primary custodian and the governing rule
The text states the mother is most entitled (أحق بالولد أمه) and this holds before and after separation unless she is disqualified.
Look for the key phrase 'أحق بالولد أمه' and the exceptive clauses.
2
Extract the disqualifying conditions
The mother loses her right if she is an apostate (مرتدة) or a sinful untrustworthy woman (فاجرة غير مأمونة), or if she marries a non-mahram.
The text uses 'إلا أن تكون' and 'ما لم تتزوج' to indicate exceptions.
3
Analyze the hadith proof
The Prophet's statement 'أنت أحق به ما لم تتزوجي' directly establishes the mother's priority and the condition of marriage. Note the hadith is ahad but its meaning is definitive (qati' al-dalala).
The hadith is cited in the text; focus on the wajh al-dalalah.
4
Understand the effect of marriage to a mahram
If the woman marries a man who is a mahram to the child (e.g., grandfather, uncle), her right is not forfeited. The text contrasts this with marriage to a stranger.
The exception is explicitly mentioned: 'بخلاف ما إذا كان الزوج ذا للصغير'.
5
Recognize the mother's entitlement to payment
The mother is not compelled to custody unless no other mahram exists, and she is entitled to payment for custody separate from breastfeeding and maintenance.
The text states: 'تستحق الأم الأجرة على الحضانة'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب الحضانة (أي في بيان أحكامها) وهي التربية يقال: حضنته حضانة إذا رفعته وربيته (مسكين) لما ذكر ثبوت النسب بعد أحوال العدة ذكر من يكون عنده الولد؛ لأن الحضانة من حقوق النسب، فالحضانة بالفتح والكسر مأخوذة من الحضن وهو ما دون الإبط إلى الكشح، وحضنا الشيء جانباه، ويقال: حضن الطائر بيضه يحضنه إذا ضمه إلى نفسه تحت جناحه، وكأن المربي للولد يتخذه في حضنه وإلى جانبه، وهي تكفل المرأة لتربيته. (فتح، عيني)
أحق بالولد أمه أي أحق الناس بالولد الصغير حضانة الصغير. (ط) قبل الفرقة وبعدها : [إلا أن تكون مرتدة أو فاجرة غير مأمونة ما لم تتزوج بزوج آخر بالإجماع. (ط،ع)] أي حق الحضانة للأم سواء طلقت أو لا ما لم تتزوج بزوج آخر بالإجماع، إلا أن تكون مرتدة أو فاجرة، والأصل فيه ما روي أن امرأة أتت عند رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم فقالت: يا رسول الله إن ابني هذا كان بطني له وعاء، وحجري له حواء، وثديي له سقاء، وزعم أبوه أنه ينتزعه مني، فقال علي: "أنت أحق به ما لم تتزوجي" "، ولأن الأم أشفق وأقدر على الحضانة، فكان الدفع إليها أنظر ، ولا تجبر على الحضانة في الصحيح؛ لاحتمال عجزها إلا أن لا يكون للولد ذو رحم محرم غير الأم، فحينئذ تجبر على حضانته؛ كي لا يضيع الولد بخلاف الأب حيث يجبر على أخذه إذا امتنع بعد الاستغناء عن الأم؛ لأن نفقته واجبة عليه.
فرع: تستحق الأم الأجرة على الحضانة حيث لم تقم منكوحة ولا معتدة فيجب على الأب ثلاثة أشياء: أجرة الرضاع، وأجرة الحضانة، ونفقة الولد. (عيني، فتح، مستخلص)
تستفاد
ثم أم الأم إذا لم يكن للولد أم بأن ماتت أو تزوجت. (ع)] أي إذا لم يكن للولد أم بأن كانت ميتة أو ليست أهلاً للحضانة أو لم تقبل الولد أو أسقطت حقها أو تزوجت بأجنبي فأم الأم أحق بالولد؛ لأن هذه الولاية من قبل الأمهات، فكانت مقدمة وإن بعدت رمز الحقائق: ۳۰۷/۱] (فتح) ثم أم الأب: أي بعد أم الأم أحق بالولد أم الأب وإن علت وقال زفر الخالة مقدمة؛ لأنها من قوم الأم، فهي أولى، وبه قال مالك في رواية، وهو رواية عن محمد عن أبي حنيفة ولنا أنها من الأمهات، ولهذا تحرز ميراث الأمهات السدس، ولأنها أوفر شفقة، ولأنها أصل الولد رمز الحقائق: ۳۰۸/۱] (فتح) الأخت لأب وأم: أي هي أحق تقديماً بعد أم لأب للإشفاق. (ع) ثم لأم: أي بعدها الأخت لأم أحق؛ لأنها من قوم الأم. (ع)
ثم لأب: أي بعد الأخت لأم، الأخت لأب أحق بالولد، وعند الشافعي في الجديد وأحمد: هي أحق الأخت من لأم لقرب القرابة، وعند زفر : هما تشتركان؛ لأنهما تستويان في الإدلاء بالأم، وفي رواية: الخالة تقدم على الأخت لأب؛ لقوله عليه: "الخالة والدة" ، وبنات الأخت لأب وأم أو لأم أولى من الخالات، واختلفت الروايات في بنات الأخت لأب والأصح أن الخالة أولى منهن وبنات الأخت أولى من بنات الأخ، وإذا اجتمع من له حق الحضانة في درجة فأورعهم أولى ثم أكبرهم رمز الحقائق: ١/٣٠٨] (فتح) ثم الخالاتُ كذلك أي بعد المذكورات الخالات ينزلن كالأخوات فمن كانت لأب وأم فهي أولى ثم لأم ثم لأب. (ع) ثم العمات كذلك: [ أي بعد الخالات أحق بالحضانة العمات كالترتيب المذكور. (ع)] ومن كانت لأب وأم فهي أولى ثم لأم ثم لأب، وبعدهن خالة الأم الشقيقة، ثم لأم ثم لأب، ثم عماتها كذلك، وخالة الأم أولى خالة الأب، ثم خالات الأب وعماته كذلك، وأما بنات الأعمام والعمات والأخوال والخالات فلا حق من لهن في الحضانة؛ لأن قرابتهن لم تتأكد بالمحرمية. (فتح، عيني) سقط حقها [ أي في الحضانة لوجود الضرر حينئذ من جهة زوج الأم . (ع)] أي كل امرأة من هؤلاء اللاتي لهن حق في الحضانة إذا تزوجت بغير محرم الصغير سقط حقها في الحضانة؛ لقوله علية: "أنت أحق به ما لم تتزوجي"، وقيد بغير المحرم؛ لعدم الشفقة فإنه ينفق على الولد قليلاً وينظر إليه مبغضاً، بخلاف ما إذا كان الزوج ذا للصغير كالجدة إذا كان زوجها الجد، أو الأم إذا كان زوجها عم الصغير، أو الخالة إذا كان زوجها عمه أو أخاه، أو العمة إذا كان زوجها خاله أو أخاه من أمه لا يسقط حقها؛ لانتفاء الضرر عن الصغير لقيام الشفقة. (مستخلص، عيني) ثم يعود بالفرقة : [ بعد ما سقط بالتزوج لزوال المانع. (ع)] أي من سقط حقها بالتزوج يعود حقها إذا ارتفعت الزوجية؛ لأن المانع قد زال كالناشزة يسقط حقها، ثم إذا عادت إلى منزل الزوج تجب النفقة، وكذا الولاية تزول بالجنون والارتداد، ثم إذا زال ذلك عادت الولاية، ثم إذا كان الطلاق رجعياً لا يعود حقها حتى تنقضي عدتها لقيام الزوجية. (فتح، مستخلص، عيني) ثم العصبات بترتيبهم : [ أي بعد هؤلاء المذكورات الأحق بالولد العصبات (ع)] أي إن لم يكن للصبي امرأة من أهل الحضانة، واختصم فيه الرجال، فأولاهم بالحضانة العصبات بترتيب الإرث يقدم الأقرب فالأقرب، فيقدم الأب ثم الجد، ثم الأخ الشقيق، ثم الأب ثم بنوه كذلك، ثم العم، ثم بنوه، وإذا اجتمعوا فالأورع ثم الأسن، غير أن الصغيرة لا تدفع إلى غير المحرم من الأقارب كابن العم ولا للأم التي ليس بمأمونة، ولا للعصبة الفاسق تحرزاً عن الفتنة، بخلاف الغلام، وإذا لم يكن للصغير عصبة يدفع إلى ذوي الأرحام عند أبي حنيفة؛ لأن لهم ولاية الإنكاح عنده، فكذا الحضانة (عيني، مستخلص، فتح)
Chapter of Custody - Meaning: explaining its rulings. Custody is upbringing. It is said: I raised him (hadanahu) if I lifted and raised him. Since the establishment of lineage after the rules of waiting period was mentioned, he mentions who will have the child, because custody is from the rights of lineage. Custody (with fatha and kasra) is derived from 'hign' which is what is below the armpit to the flank, and the two sides of a thing are its 'hidnan'. It is said: the bird broods its eggs (yahdinahu) if it gathers them under its wing. It is as if the caretaker of the child takes him in his lap and beside him. It is the woman undertaking to raise him. (Fath, 'Ayni)
The mother is more entitled to the child – meaning the most entitled of people to the young child regarding his custody. (T) Before separation and after it: [Unless she is an apostate or a sinful woman who is not trustworthy, as long as she does not marry another husband, by consensus. (T, 'A)] Meaning: The right of custody belongs to the mother whether she is divorced or not, as long as she does not marry another husband, by consensus, unless she is an apostate or a sinful woman. The basis for this is what is narrated that a woman came to the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) and said: O Messenger of Allah, this son of mine – my belly was a vessel for him, my lap was a home for him, and my breast was a watering place for him, and his father claims that he will take him from me. He said: 'You are more entitled to him as long as you do not marry.' And because the mother is more compassionate and more capable of custody, so giving him to her is more beneficial. She is not compelled to custody in the correct view due to the possibility of her inability, unless the child has no mahram relative other than the mother, then she is compelled to his custody so that the child is not lost – contrary to the father, who is compelled to take him if he refuses after the child no longer needs the mother, because his maintenance is obligatory upon him.
Branch: The mother is entitled to payment for custody if she is not a married woman or in waiting period. The father must pay three things: payment for breastfeeding, payment for custody, and the child's maintenance. ('Ayni, Fath, Mustakhlas)
Benefited.
Then the maternal grandmother – if the child has no mother, whether she died or married. ('A) Meaning: If the child has no mother, whether she is dead, or not suitable for custody, or did not accept the child, or waived her right, or married a stranger, then the maternal grandmother is more entitled to the child. Because this authority is from the maternal side, so she is preferred even if distant. (Fath, Rami al-Haqa'iq 1/307) Then the paternal grandmother – i.e., after the maternal grandmother, the paternal grandmother is more entitled to the child, even if higher. Zufar said the maternal aunt is preferred because she is from the mother's people, so she is more entitled. Malik said the same in a narration, and it is a narration from Muhammad from Abu Hanifah. Our proof: she (paternal grandmother) is from the mothers, so she inherits the sixth of the mothers' inheritance, and because she is more compassionate, and because she is the origin of the child. (Fath, Rami al-Haqa'iq 1/308) The full sister (german sister) – i.e., she is more entitled after the paternal grandmother due to compassion. ('A) Then the uterine sister – i.e., after her, the uterine sister is more entitled because she is from the mother's people. ('A)
Then the consanguine sister – i.e., after the uterine sister, the consanguine sister is more entitled to the child. According to al-Shafi'i in the new view and Ahmad, she is more entitled than the uterine sister due to closer kinship. According to Zufar, they share equally because they both trace through the mother. In one narration, the maternal aunt is preferred over the consanguine sister because of his saying: 'The maternal aunt is a mother.' The daughters of the consanguine or uterine sister are more entitled than maternal aunts. Narrations differ regarding daughters of the consanguine sister; the correct view is that the maternal aunt is more entitled than them, and daughters of the sister are more entitled than daughters of the brother. If those who have the right to custody are on the same level, then the most pious among them is first, then the oldest. (Fath, Rami al-Haqa'iq 1/308) Then the maternal aunts likewise – meaning after the aforementioned, the maternal aunts descend like the sisters; so the one from parents (full maternal aunt) is first, then uterine, then consanguine. ('A) Then the paternal aunts likewise – i.e., after the maternal aunts, the paternal aunts are more entitled to custody in the same order. ('A) Then the one from parents is first, then uterine, then consanguine. After them, the maternal aunt of the mother (full sister), then uterine, then consanguine, then her paternal aunts likewise. The maternal aunt of the mother is more entitled than the maternal aunt of the father, then the maternal aunts of the father and his paternal aunts likewise. As for the daughters of paternal uncles, paternal aunts, maternal uncles, and maternal aunts – they have no right to custody because their kinship is not confirmed by mahram status. (Fath, 'Ayni) Her right is forfeited – i.e., in custody due to the existence of harm from the husband of the mother. ('A) Meaning: Every woman among those who have a right to custody, if she marries a non-mahram of the child, her right to custody is forfeited due to his saying: 'You are more entitled to him as long as you do not marry.' The restriction to non-mahram is due to lack of compassion, for he spends little on the child and looks at him with hatred – contrary to if the husband is a mahram to the child, like the grandmother if her husband is the grandfather, or the mother if her husband is the child's paternal uncle, or the maternal aunt if her husband is her paternal uncle or brother, or the paternal aunt if her husband is her maternal uncle or her brother from the mother – then her right is not forfeited due to the absence of harm to the child because compassion exists. (Mustakhlas, 'Ayni) Then it returns through separation – i.e., after it was forfeited by marriage, due to removal of the impediment. ('A) Meaning: Whoever's right was forfeited by marriage, her right returns when the marriage ends because the impediment is removed – like the Nashizah (disobedient wife) whose right is forfeited, then if she returns to the husband's home, maintenance becomes obligatory. Similarly, guardianship ceases due to insanity and apostasy, then when that is removed, guardianship returns. However, if the divorce is revocable, her right does not return until her waiting period ends because the marriage continues. (Fath, Mustakhlas, 'Ayni) Then the 'asabat (agnatic heirs) in their order – i.e., after these aforementioned women, the 'asabat are most entitled to the child. ('A) Meaning: If the child has no woman from the custodians, and the men dispute, then the most entitled to custody among them are the 'asabat in the order of inheritance – the closest is preferred, then the next. So the father is preferred, then the grandfather, then the full brother, then the consanguine brother, then their sons likewise, then the paternal uncle, then his sons. If they are on the same level, then the most pious, then the elder. However, a young girl is not given to a non-mahram relative like a cousin, nor to a mother who is not trustworthy, nor to a sinful 'asabah, to avoid temptation – contrary to a boy. If the child has no 'asabah, then he is given to dhawu al-arham (uterine relatives) according to Abu Hanifah, because they have authority over marriage in his view, so likewise custody. ('Ayni, Mustakhlas, Fath)
Source pages p. 520

Commentary
This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq, with commentary from al-'Ayni and al-Fath, establishes the Hanafi hierarchy of custodians (hadanah) for a minor child. The text begins by defining hadanah linguistically and legally, then states the primary rule: the mother is most entitled before and after divorce, as long as she does not marry a stranger, is not an apostate, and is not sinful/untrustworthy. The proof is the well-known hadith where the Prophet (peace be upon him) ruled that the mother is more entitled as long as she does not marry. The mother is not compelled to take custody unless no other mahram relative exists. A branch ruling clarifies that the mother is entitled to payment for custody separate from breastfeeding and maintenance.
The order continues: if the mother is absent or disqualified, custody goes to the maternal grandmother, then the paternal grandmother (even if ascended), then the full sister, then the uterine sister, then the consanguine sister. The text notes a difference with Zufar and Malik who prefer the maternal aunt over the paternal grandmother, but the Hanafi position is that the paternal grandmother is preferred because she is from the mothers and inherits the sixth. Then come maternal aunts, then paternal aunts, each in order of full, uterine, consanguine. Daughters of uncles and aunts have no custody right because their kinship is not mahram.
The passage then discusses loss of custody: if a female custodian marries a non-mahram, her right is forfeited due to lack of compassion, but if she marries a mahram (e.g., grandmother marries grandfather), her right remains. The right returns upon separation (death or divorce) from that marriage, except in revocable divorce where it returns only after the waiting period.
Finally, if no female custodian exists, custody goes to male 'asabat (agnates) in the order of inheritance: father, grandfather, brother, uncle, etc. Among them, the most pious and then the oldest are preferred. Young girls are not given to non-mahram relatives. If no 'asabah exists, Abu Hanifah gives custody to dhawu al-arham (uterine relatives), analogizing from their authority in marriage.

Key Terms
الحضانة (al-ḥaḍānah): The legal right and duty to care for and raise a minor child, including physical custody and upbringing.
محرم (maḥram): A person whom the child cannot marry due to close blood relationship or fosterage, such as father, brother, grandfather, etc.
عصبات (ʿaṣabāt): Agnatic male heirs who inherit by virtue of being male relatives through males, such as father, brother, uncle.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the hadith cited in the text, what condition is placed on the mother's right to custody?
A) She must not be divorced.
B) She must not marry a non-mahram.
C) She must be wealthy.
D) She must live with the father.

Key Takeaway
The mother is the primary custodian unless she is apostate, sinful, or married to a non-mahram; her right returns if the marriage ends.

Talaq — Divorce
intermediate
10 min
The Order of Custodians: Female Relatives and Male Agnates
Establishes the hierarchical order of custodians for a child.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to recall the hierarchical order of female custodians after the mother in Hanafi law and explain the intra-madhhab dispute regarding the paternal grandmother versus the maternal aunt.

Core Idea
After the mother, custody goes to maternal grandmother, then paternal grandmother, then sisters, then aunts; male agnates only if no qualified female.

The previous lesson established the mother's right. This lesson details the cascade of female relatives who qualify for custody in her absence, the conditions that forfeit and restore their right, and finally the transfer to male agnates. We also examine a notable intra-Hanafi dispute between Zufar and the school's relied-upon position.

Guided Path
1
List the female custodians in order
The text gives a specific sequence: mother → maternal grandmother → paternal grandmother → full sister → uterine sister → consanguine sister → maternal aunts → paternal aunts → then more distant relatives like maternal aunt of the mother, etc.
Note that the maternal side is generally preferred over the paternal side in many steps.
2
Note the reasoning behind the order
The order is based on closeness of relation, compassion (shafaqah), and inheritance principles. For example, the paternal grandmother is preferred over the maternal aunt because she is from the mothers and inherits the sixth.
This reasoning is used in the Hanafi response to Zufar's dispute.
3
Analyze the intra-Hanafi dispute: Zufar vs. the majority
Zufar holds that the maternal aunt (khala) is preferred over the paternal grandmother. The majority (including Abu Hanifah, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad in the relied-upon view) hold the paternal grandmother first. Understand each side's dalil.
The text presents the dispute and then gives the Hanafi evidence (lana).
4
Identify the conditions for loss and return of the right
Any female custodian who marries a non-mahram loses her right, and it returns upon separation. Marriage to a mahram does not forfeit. Also, apostasy and sinfulness cause loss. These rules apply to all female custodians.
The text explicitly states: 'سقط حقها... إذا تزوجت بغير محرم' and 'ثم يعود بالفرقة'.
5
Determine the male custodians after females
If no qualified female custodian exists, custody goes to male 'asabat (agnatic heirs) in the order of inheritance: father, grandfather, brother, uncle, etc. If no 'asabah, Abu Hanifah gives it to dhawu al-arham (uterine relatives).
The text ends with: 'ثم العصبات بترتيبهم' and then 'إذا لم يكن للصغير عصبة يدفع إلى ذوي الأرحام'.

(ع)] أي إذا لم يكن للولد أم بأن كانت ميتة أو ليست أهلاً للحضانة أو لم تقبل الولد أو أسقطت حقها أو تزوجت بأجنبي فأم الأم أحق بالولد؛ لأن هذه الولاية من قبل الأمهات، فكانت مقدمة وإن بعدت رمز الحقائق: ۳۰۷/۱] (فتح) ثم أم الأب: أي بعد أم الأم أحق بالولد أم الأب وإن علت وقال زفر الخالة مقدمة؛ لأنها من قوم الأم، فهي أولى، وبه قال مالك في رواية، وهو رواية عن محمد عن أبي حنيفة ولنا أنها من الأمهات، ولهذا تحرز ميراث الأمهات السدس، ولأنها أوفر شفقة، ولأنها أصل الولد رمز الحقائق: ۳۰۸/۱] (فتح) الأخت لأب وأم: أي هي أحق تقديماً بعد أم لأب للإشفاق. (ع) ثم لأم: أي بعدها الأخت لأم أحق؛ لأنها من قوم الأم. (ع)
ثم لأب: أي بعد الأخت لأم، الأخت لأب أحق بالولد، وعند الشافعي في الجديد وأحمد: هي أحق الأخت من لأم لقرب القرابة، وعند زفر : هما تشتركان؛ لأنهما تستويان في الإدلاء بالأم، وفي رواية: الخالة تقدم على الأخت لأب؛ لقوله عليه: "الخالة والدة" ، وبنات الأخت لأب وأم أو لأم أولى من الخالات، واختلفت الروايات في بنات الأخت لأب والأصح أن الخالة أولى منهن وبنات الأخت أولى من بنات الأخ، وإذا اجتمع من له حق الحضانة في درجة فأورعهم أولى ثم أكبرهم رمز الحقائق: ١/٣٠٨] (فتح) ثم الخالاتُ كذلك أي بعد المذكورات الخالات ينزلن كالأخوات فمن كانت لأب وأم فهي أولى ثم لأم ثم لأب. (ع) ثم العمات كذلك: [ أي بعد الخالات أحق بالحضانة العمات كالترتيب المذكور. (ع)] ومن كانت لأب وأم فهي أولى ثم لأم ثم لأب، وبعدهن خالة الأم الشقيقة، ثم لأم ثم لأب، ثم عماتها كذلك، وخالة الأم أولى خالة الأب، ثم خالات الأب وعماته كذلك، وأما بنات الأعمام والعمات والأخوال والخالات فلا حق من لهن في الحضانة؛ لأن قرابتهن لم تتأكد بالمحرمية. (فتح، عيني) سقط حقها [ أي في الحضانة لوجود الضرر حينئذ من جهة زوج الأم . (ع)] أي كل امرأة من هؤلاء اللاتي لهن حق في الحضانة إذا تزوجت بغير محرم الصغير سقط حقها في الحضانة؛ لقوله علية: "أنت أحق به ما لم تتزوجي"، وقيد بغير المحرم؛ لعدم الشفقة فإنه ينفق على الولد قليلاً وينظر إليه مبغضاً، بخلاف ما إذا كان الزوج ذا للصغير كالجدة إذا كان زوجها الجد، أو الأم إذا كان زوجها عم الصغير، أو الخالة إذا كان زوجها عمه أو أخاه، أو العمة إذا كان زوجها خاله أو أخاه من أمه لا يسقط حقها؛ لانتفاء الضرر عن الصغير لقيام الشفقة. (مستخلص، عيني) ثم يعود بالفرقة : [ بعد ما سقط بالتزوج لزوال المانع. (ع)] أي من سقط حقها بالتزوج يعود حقها إذا ارتفعت الزوجية؛ لأن المانع قد زال كالناشزة يسقط حقها، ثم إذا عادت إلى منزل الزوج تجب النفقة، وكذا الولاية تزول بالجنون والارتداد، ثم إذا زال ذلك عادت الولاية، ثم إذا كان الطلاق رجعياً لا يعود حقها حتى تنقضي عدتها لقيام الزوجية. (فتح، مستخلص، عيني) ثم العصبات بترتيبهم : [ أي بعد هؤلاء المذكورات الأحق بالولد العصبات (ع)] أي إن لم يكن للصبي امرأة من أهل الحضانة، واختصم فيه الرجال، فأولاهم بالحضانة العصبات بترتيب الإرث يقدم الأقرب فالأقرب، فيقدم الأب ثم الجد، ثم الأخ الشقيق، ثم الأب ثم بنوه كذلك، ثم العم، ثم بنوه، وإذا اجتمعوا فالأورع ثم الأسن، غير أن الصغيرة لا تدفع إلى غير المحرم من الأقارب كابن العم ولا للأم التي ليس بمأمونة، ولا للعصبة الفاسق تحرزاً عن الفتنة، بخلاف الغلام، وإذا لم يكن للصغير عصبة يدفع إلى ذوي الأرحام عند أبي حنيفة؛ لأن لهم ولاية الإنكاح عنده، فكذا الحضانة (عيني، مستخلص، فتح)
Chapter of Custody - Meaning: explaining its rulings. Custody is upbringing. It is said: I raised him (hadanahu) if I lifted and raised him. Since the establishment of lineage after the rules of waiting period was mentioned, he mentions who will have the child, because custody is from the rights of lineage. Custody (with fatha and kasra) is derived from 'hign' which is what is below the armpit to the flank, and the two sides of a thing are its 'hidnan'. It is said: the bird broods its eggs (yahdinahu) if it gathers them under its wing. It is as if the caretaker of the child takes him in his lap and beside him. It is the woman undertaking to raise him. (Fath, 'Ayni)
The mother is more entitled to the child – meaning the most entitled of people to the young child regarding his custody. (T) Before separation and after it: [Unless she is an apostate or a sinful woman who is not trustworthy, as long as she does not marry another husband, by consensus. (T, 'A)] Meaning: The right of custody belongs to the mother whether she is divorced or not, as long as she does not marry another husband, by consensus, unless she is an apostate or a sinful woman. The basis for this is what is narrated that a woman came to the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) and said: O Messenger of Allah, this son of mine – my belly was a vessel for him, my lap was a home for him, and my breast was a watering place for him, and his father claims that he will take him from me. He said: 'You are more entitled to him as long as you do not marry.' And because the mother is more compassionate and more capable of custody, so giving him to her is more beneficial. She is not compelled to custody in the correct view due to the possibility of her inability, unless the child has no mahram relative other than the mother, then she is compelled to his custody so that the child is not lost – contrary to the father, who is compelled to take him if he refuses after the child no longer needs the mother, because his maintenance is obligatory upon him.
Branch: The mother is entitled to payment for custody if she is not a married woman or in waiting period. The father must pay three things: payment for breastfeeding, payment for custody, and the child's maintenance. ('Ayni, Fath, Mustakhlas)
Benefited.
Then the maternal grandmother – if the child has no mother, whether she died or married. ('A) Meaning: If the child has no mother, whether she is dead, or not suitable for custody, or did not accept the child, or waived her right, or married a stranger, then the maternal grandmother is more entitled to the child. Because this authority is from the maternal side, so she is preferred even if distant. (Fath, Rami al-Haqa'iq 1/307) Then the paternal grandmother – i.e., after the maternal grandmother, the paternal grandmother is more entitled to the child, even if higher. Zufar said the maternal aunt is preferred because she is from the mother's people, so she is more entitled. Malik said the same in a narration, and it is a narration from Muhammad from Abu Hanifah. Our proof: she (paternal grandmother) is from the mothers, so she inherits the sixth of the mothers' inheritance, and because she is more compassionate, and because she is the origin of the child. (Fath, Rami al-Haqa'iq 1/308) The full sister (german sister) – i.e., she is more entitled after the paternal grandmother due to compassion. ('A) Then the uterine sister – i.e., after her, the uterine sister is more entitled because she is from the mother's people. ('A)
Then the consanguine sister – i.e., after the uterine sister, the consanguine sister is more entitled to the child. According to al-Shafi'i in the new view and Ahmad, she is more entitled than the uterine sister due to closer kinship. According to Zufar, they share equally because they both trace through the mother. In one narration, the maternal aunt is preferred over the consanguine sister because of his saying: 'The maternal aunt is a mother.' The daughters of the consanguine or uterine sister are more entitled than maternal aunts. Narrations differ regarding daughters of the consanguine sister; the correct view is that the maternal aunt is more entitled than them, and daughters of the sister are more entitled than daughters of the brother. If those who have the right to custody are on the same level, then the most pious among them is first, then the oldest. (Fath, Rami al-Haqa'iq 1/308) Then the maternal aunts likewise – meaning after the aforementioned, the maternal aunts descend like the sisters; so the one from parents (full maternal aunt) is first, then uterine, then consanguine. ('A) Then the paternal aunts likewise – i.e., after the maternal aunts, the paternal aunts are more entitled to custody in the same order. ('A) Then the one from parents is first, then uterine, then consanguine. After them, the maternal aunt of the mother (full sister), then uterine, then consanguine, then her paternal aunts likewise. The maternal aunt of the mother is more entitled than the maternal aunt of the father, then the maternal aunts of the father and his paternal aunts likewise. As for the daughters of paternal uncles, paternal aunts, maternal uncles, and maternal aunts – they have no right to custody because their kinship is not confirmed by mahram status. (Fath, 'Ayni) Her right is forfeited – i.e., in custody due to the existence of harm from the husband of the mother. ('A) Meaning: Every woman among those who have a right to custody, if she marries a non-mahram of the child, her right to custody is forfeited due to his saying: 'You are more entitled to him as long as you do not marry.' The restriction to non-mahram is due to lack of compassion, for he spends little on the child and looks at him with hatred – contrary to if the husband is a mahram to the child, like the grandmother if her husband is the grandfather, or the mother if her husband is the child's paternal uncle, or the maternal aunt if her husband is her paternal uncle or brother, or the paternal aunt if her husband is her maternal uncle or her brother from the mother – then her right is not forfeited due to the absence of harm to the child because compassion exists. (Mustakhlas, 'Ayni) Then it returns through separation – i.e., after it was forfeited by marriage, due to removal of the impediment. ('A) Meaning: Whoever's right was forfeited by marriage, her right returns when the marriage ends because the impediment is removed – like the Nashizah (disobedient wife) whose right is forfeited, then if she returns to the husband's home, maintenance becomes obligatory. Similarly, guardianship ceases due to insanity and apostasy, then when that is removed, guardianship returns. However, if the divorce is revocable, her right does not return until her waiting period ends because the marriage continues. (Fath, Mustakhlas, 'Ayni) Then the 'asabat (agnatic heirs) in their order – i.e., after these aforementioned women, the 'asabat are most entitled to the child. ('A) Meaning: If the child has no woman from the custodians, and the men dispute, then the most entitled to custody among them are the 'asabat in the order of inheritance – the closest is preferred, then the next. So the father is preferred, then the grandfather, then the full brother, then the consanguine brother, then their sons likewise, then the paternal uncle, then his sons. If they are on the same level, then the most pious, then the elder. However, a young girl is not given to a non-mahram relative like a cousin, nor to a mother who is not trustworthy, nor to a sinful 'asabah, to avoid temptation – contrary to a boy. If the child has no 'asabah, then he is given to dhawu al-arham (uterine relatives) according to Abu Hanifah, because they have authority over marriage in his view, so likewise custody. ('Ayni, Mustakhlas, Fath)
Source pages p. 520

Commentary
This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq, with commentary from al-'Ayni and al-Fath, establishes the Hanafi hierarchy of custodians (hadanah) for a minor child. The text begins by defining hadanah linguistically and legally, then states the primary rule: the mother is most entitled before and after divorce, as long as she does not marry a stranger, is not an apostate, and is not sinful/untrustworthy. The proof is the well-known hadith where the Prophet (peace be upon him) ruled that the mother is more entitled as long as she does not marry. The mother is not compelled to take custody unless no other mahram relative exists. A branch ruling clarifies that the mother is entitled to payment for custody separate from breastfeeding and maintenance.
The order continues: if the mother is absent or disqualified, custody goes to the maternal grandmother, then the paternal grandmother (even if ascended), then the full sister, then the uterine sister, then the consanguine sister. The text notes a difference with Zufar and Malik who prefer the maternal aunt over the paternal grandmother, but the Hanafi position is that the paternal grandmother is preferred because she is from the mothers and inherits the sixth. Then come maternal aunts, then paternal aunts, each in order of full, uterine, consanguine. Daughters of uncles and aunts have no custody right because their kinship is not mahram.
The passage then discusses loss of custody: if a female custodian marries a non-mahram, her right is forfeited due to lack of compassion, but if she marries a mahram (e.g., grandmother marries grandfather), her right remains. The right returns upon separation (death or divorce) from that marriage, except in revocable divorce where it returns only after the waiting period.
Finally, if no female custodian exists, custody goes to male 'asabat (agnates) in the order of inheritance: father, grandfather, brother, uncle, etc. Among them, the most pious and then the oldest are preferred. Young girls are not given to non-mahram relatives. If no 'asabah exists, Abu Hanifah gives custody to dhawu al-arham (uterine relatives), analogizing from their authority in marriage.

Key Terms
الحضانة (al-ḥaḍānah): The legal right and duty to care for and raise a minor child, including physical custody and upbringing.
محرم (maḥram): A person whom the child cannot marry due to close blood relationship or fosterage, such as father, brother, grandfather, etc.
عصبات (ʿaṣabāt): Agnatic male heirs who inherit by virtue of being male relatives through males, such as father, brother, uncle.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Hanafi law, what happens to a female custodian's right if she marries a man who is a mahram to the child?
A) It is forfeited.
B) It is unaffected.
C) It is transferred to her husband.
D) It becomes shared with the husband.

Key Takeaway
Custody follows a strict hierarchy: maternal grandmother, then paternal grandmother, then sisters, then aunts; men only after all qualified females; marriage to a non-mahram forfeits but right returns upon separation.
