Talaq — Divorce
intermediate
6 min
Apostasy After Final Divorce: Its Effect on Maintenance
Ruling on apostasy and its nullification of maintenance

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on maintenance when a woman apostatizes after a final divorce and distinguish it from the case of tamkin.

Core Idea
Apostasy after irrevocable divorce cancels maintenance; tamkin does not.

In this passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq, we examine a specific case: a woman who has received a final divorce (triple or bā'in) and then commits apostasy. The text clarifies that her maintenance during the 'iddah drops because she is imprisoned for apostasy. However, if she merely enables the husband's son to have intercourse with her, this does not affect maintenance. The distinction lies in the legal consequence of imprisonment.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and condition
The act is apostasy after a final divorce (batt). Condition: the divorce is irrevocable (triple or bā'in).
Batt means final separation.
2
State the ruling
Maintenance drops (sāqit) immediately upon apostasy.
3
Understand the rationale
The apostate woman is imprisoned until she repents; a prisoner is not entitled to maintenance because she is not confined for the husband's right.
The 'iddah continues but maintenance is suspended.
4
Distinguish from tamkin
If she enables the husband's son to have intercourse, maintenance does not drop because the separation is already final and she is not imprisoned.
Tamkin does not constitute nushuz in this context.
5
Note special cases
If she returns to Islam and the husband's home, maintenance resumes. If she fled to dar al-harb as an apostate, maintenance is permanently lost.
Flight terminates the 'iddah legally.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وردتها بعد البت إلخ [ أي الطلاق الثلاث أو الواحدة البائنة. (ط)] أي إذا طلق الرجل امرأته ثلاثاً أو واحدة بائنة ثم ارتدت سقط نفقتها؛ لأن المرتدة تحبس حتى تتوب ولا نفقة للمحبوسة، وقوله: "لا تمكين ابنه"، أي إن مكنت ابن زوجها للوطء بها بعد البينونة بالطلاق لا تسقط نفقتها؛ لأن الفرقة ثبت بالطلاق، ولا يعمل فيه الردة، ولا التمكين؛ لأن الممكنة لا تستحق الحبس، فافترقا حتى لو أسلمت المرأة وعادت إلى منزل الزوج وجبت لها النفقة كالناشزة إذا رجعت ولو لحقت بدار الحرب مرتدة ثم عادت مسلمة فلا نفقة لها كيف ما كان؛ لسقوط العدة باللحاق حكماً لتباين الدارين (مستخلص عيني) نفقتها : إذا حبست لتثوب فإن كانت في بيت زوجها فلها النفقة. (ع)
And her apostasy after the final [divorce]—i.e., triple divorce or one irrevocable divorce—i.e., if a man divorces his wife three times or one irrevocable divorce, then she apostatizes, her maintenance drops, because the apostate woman is imprisoned until she repents, and there is no maintenance for the imprisoned woman. And his saying: 'nor does enabling his son [nullify maintenance]'—i.e., if she enables the husband's son to have intercourse with her after the irrevocability of divorce, her maintenance does not drop, because the separation was established by divorce, and apostasy does not affect it, nor does enabling, because the one who enables [herself] is not entitled to confinement, so the two cases differ. Even if the woman becomes Muslim and returns to the husband's home, her maintenance becomes wajib, like the nashiz when she returns. And if she fled to the abode of war as an apostate then returned as Muslim, she has no maintenance at all, because the 'iddah dropped by her arrival there legally due to the separation of the two abodes. (Mukhtasar 'Ayni) Her maintenance: if she is imprisoned to repent, if she is in her husband's house, she has maintenance. ('Ayni)
Source pages p. 531

Commentary
This ruling addresses how apostasy after a final divorce (triple or bā'in) affects maintenance. The Hanafi position is that if a woman apostatizes after the divorce becomes irrevocable, her maintenance ceases immediately because an apostate is imprisoned and therefore not entitled to maintenance, as she is not confined for the husband's right. However, if she merely enables the husband's son (or any other) to have intercourse with her after the divorce, this does not cancel her maintenance because the separation is already finalized by divorce, and her action does not affect the 'iddah. The two cases are distinguished: apostasy nullifies maintenance because she is legally imprisoned; tamkīn does not because she is not imprisoned. If she returns to Islam and to the husband's home, maintenance resumes, analogous to a nashiz who returns. A special case: if she flees to Dār al-Ḥarb as an apostate and later returns as Muslim, she receives no maintenance at all because her 'iddah was legally terminated by the separation of abodes (ikhtilāf al-dārayn). The commentary from 'Ayni adds: if she is imprisoned (to repent) and is in her husband's house, she does receive maintenance.

Key Terms
البت (al-batt): A final, irrevocable divorce, whether triple or a single bā'in talāq.
تمكين ابنه (tamkīn ibnihi): The divorcée allowing the husband's son (from another wife) to have sexual intercourse with her after the divorce has become final.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A woman is divorced triple (bā'in) and then commits apostasy. According to the Hanafi school, what happens to her maintenance?
A) Maintenance continues as usual.
B) Maintenance stops because she is imprisoned for apostasy.
C) Maintenance stops only if she flees to enemy territory.
D) Maintenance is reduced by half.

Key Takeaway
Apostasy after final divorce drops maintenance due to imprisonment; tamkin does not.
